Roosevelt's Fishing Trip Returns to the Palace, Narrowly Escaping Misfortune on the Way; Car Almost Collides with Train; Luckily Driver Was Alert; Important Bills Such as Silver Tariffs to Have Fierce Battles Between the Government and Congress 35

Miami City. Roosevelt, on a yacht, fished and traveled around the Bahamas for two weeks. Now that his vacation is over, he has taken a special train from here to return to Washington, D.C. to resume his administration. (12th Havas Dispatch)

Miami. President Roosevelt passed through here today and went straight back to Washington. He narrowly escaped misfortune on the way, no different from escaping death. According to those who told people afterward, they still had lingering fears. Roosevelt landed from the dock today and went straight to the station to board the special train. Among those who accompanied him were General Johnson, the Director of the Reconstruction Office, and Li Mai, the secretary, as well as many White House correspondents. They were all in a large car driving straight to the station. Unexpectedly, a train suddenly came at a crossroads. The two cars were almost close to colliding. Fortunately, the train driver came to his senses and hurriedly turned the train into another track. The large car was spared from the disaster. According to reporters, Roosevelt's face has turned dark after two weeks of fishing, because it was exposed to the sun and heat. (12th National Telegram)

(Washington) The important issues that President Roosevelt will encounter after returning to the White House tomorrow are tariffs, silver, taxes, and the Exchange Management Act. The most important action in the Senate in the two weeks since President Roosevelt's trip was the legislation to formulate the budget case for independent agencies, to restore salary cuts and veterans' pensions, and to defeat the president's veto. According to administrative leaders, the president feels that the country must increase tax revenue to make up for the burden on the government since the enactment of that law. Whether the government authorities are satisfied with the tax bills in the Senate and the House of Representatives is still uncertain. Although ordinary administrative policies can be exercised without hindrance, there may be changes due to the increase in veterans' pensions and official salaries. The Silver Act, which President Roosevelt requested the current Congress to postpone, is still on the horizon in Congress. The Senate has now completed the mixed silver bill that gathers the major clauses in the Dais case, the Weiler amendment, and the Thomas plan. There is a good chance that the case will pass. The "Phillips-Rayburn" Exchange Management Act, which President Roosevelt regards as an important plan, will soon be voted on by the two houses. The House of Representatives' state subcommittee amended the case today and determined a minimum margin of 40%, which is 15% less than the original case. The minimum margin and the management agency established by the government are the main points of contention between the opposing and supporting parties in the case. The progress of the tariff case has not been as fast as the government had hoped. The case has not yet been voted on by the two houses. The original intention of the case was to authorize President Roosevelt to sign reciprocal trade agreements with foreign countries. (12th National Telegram)

(Washington) A fierce battle between the Senate and President Roosevelt will break out soon. There are three bills in Congress, all supported by the two houses, that will undermine President Roosevelt's plan to avoid lowering the price of the dollar. The first is the Dais case, which conflicts with the government's policy of not starting the silver issue until the results of the plan to reduce the gold composition of the dollar are fully ascertained. The second is the McLeod case, which advocates that the government should compensate for deposits of less than $2,500 in banks that closed after January 1930, which amounts to hundreds of millions. Depositors are now writing to members of Congress, asking for assistance. Because Congress will have elections in the fall, members tend to show favor to depositors. The third is the Frazier-Lemke case, which advocates providing financial assistance for rural mortgages. If this case passes, the government will inevitably issue hundreds of millions of paper money. Although the public believes that the case has almost no hope of being passed, it is known that President Roosevelt will veto it.

(12th Reuters Telegram)

(Washington) Bella, an advisor to the Senate Banking Committee, recently sent blank forms to brokers on the exchange, asking them to fill in item by item the names of those who buy and sell silver and trade silver speculation, the inventory of each household, and its position in the market. According to the current Senate's advocacy of minting silver coins, it seems that it has decided to fight openly with President Roosevelt. Therefore, some people believe that this investigation seems to be authorized by government personnel who oppose the minting of silver coins, so as to understand who will profit after the minting of silver coins, and then there can be an excuse to deal with those who generally advocate the minting of silver coins. (13th Havas News Agency Telegram)

Issuance of Lottery Bonds Rejected by House of Representatives 36

(Washington) Speaker of the House of Representatives Rayner today rejected Kenna's proposal to hold national lottery bonds and raise 100 million gold dollars. (The case was drafted by adopting the lottery bond methods of countries such as ancient China, Cuba, and France.) Mr. Huo has decided to abolish this case, because the current situation in the United States has not reached the point where it cannot maintain its finances without seeking equal income. (12th National News Agency Telegram)

Senate Forms Committee to Investigate Arms Manufacturing and Trade 37

(Washington) The Senate today decided to organize a seven-member committee to start investigating the manufacture and trade of arms and ammunition in the fall, in order to implement legislation to prevent profiteering during wartime. (13th Reuters Telegram)

(Washington) The Senate today adopted the resolutions of Nai and Vandenberg, appointing a special committee of seven people to investigate the manufacture of arms in the United States. The resolution is related to President Roosevelt's request to declare an embargo on arms exports. The president requested this power because he wanted to prevent the transportation of arms to one or more countries that endanger world peace. (13th National Telegram)

Labor Strikes Spread Throughout the Land; Tax Resistance Waves Rise Again in Pennsylvania 38

Eighteen thousand automobile parts workers in Detroit are dissatisfied with the procedures adopted by the Labor Bureau and have threatened to strike at midnight tonight if their demands for reduced working hours and increased wages are not met. Labor leaders and representatives from the Reconstruction Office have been working hard in the past 48 hours to try to resolve this dispute, but to no avail. Typists, letter carriers, elevator operators, and others have started striking today, as if an epidemic is spreading. The labor climate is getting worse, and it is feared that the authorities' efforts in the last five minutes may not be able to reverse the labor strike tonight.

Three thousand eight hundred workers from forty-five automobile parts factories in Detroit City have started striking since midnight this morning. Also, the Nash automobile factory in Qwashacheng, Wisconsin, has resumed work after a six-week strike. (12th Havas Telegram)

Labor strikes in Philadelphia are surging. Brawls have occurred openly, resulting in dozens of injuries and more than sixty arrests. The situation in the Alabama coal mining area is particularly tense. Some miners who are willing to resume work have been shot by strikers. The president of the United Mine Workers of America openly threatened that if the mine owners still do not comply with the Economic Recovery Administration's methods of reducing working hours and increasing wages, they will not hesitate to cause internal unrest, and declared that the miners are all prepared and can listen to the President's dispatch with 20 divisions of armed workers within 15 days to force the mine owners to concede and allow the minimum wage set by the Reconstruction Office. (12th Havas Telegram)

Pottsville. In Pottsville, Pennsylvania, USA, today, thousands of taxpayers were angry because the tax assessment was too high, some as high as three times the original. The property valuation committee refused to hold a public inquiry. They broke open the money door of the committee room, forcibly dragged the committee members into the public inquiry room, smashed all the glass windows, overturned the tables and desks, and trampled on the committee members. The situation began to ease slightly after the police suppressed it. The committee members were extremely frightened and finally agreed to listen to the statements of the 12 district delegations. The taxpayers were satisfied and dispersed. (12th Reuters Telegram)

Many Obstacles on the Road to Recovery; Johnson Dares Not Relax 39

Miami City. Today, Roosevelt proposed that General Johnson, the Director of the National Reconstruction Office, and Li Mai, the secretary, be given special leave to rest, because the two gentlemen have worked very hard recently and have made great contributions. Roosevelt urged the two gentlemen to get off the train halfway in Charlotte for a two-week vacation, but the two gentlemen declined and dared not take a break, saying that they were willing to assist the President in returning to the American capital quickly and continue to work as usual. (12th National Telegram)

Stimson Advocates U.S. Joining League of Nations; If Peace Organizations Are Allowed to Weaken, the Whole World Will Suffer from War 40

Former Secretary of State Stimson delivered a speech at Princeton University today, strongly urging the United States to join the League of Nations, saying that the American people are most capable of sympathizing, having courage and providing assistance to the world in the important struggles of the world without feeling difficulties or taking risks, so as to protect public civilization and stop war. The League of Nations represents European politicians directly preserving Europe and indirectly preserving the world, with meticulous efforts to avoid the harm of new wars. If we must want our government not to be involved in foreign affairs and not to participate in the peaceful efforts of other countries in the world, then we will eventually encounter a fact, that is, the strength of peace organizations will be weakened, and mankind will often encounter war. Not only will other countries in the world be harmed, but the United States and its civilization will also be poisoned. (12th Reuters Telegram)

The League of Nations is Incompetent Because of the Selfishness of Various Countries; The British Discuss International Cooperation 41

(London) Various groups supporting the International Federation of Associations held a conference today. Lord Cecil, the former British representative to the League of Nations, attended and delivered a speech, saying, "The reason why the League of Nations has developed into the current crisis phenomenon is not due to the imperfections of the League of Nations' own system, but because it is not used properly. Workers who are not skilled often blame the disadvantages of the equipment. The criticism of the League of Nations is the same. Today, the world is encountering difficulties, but the only reason is that members of the League of Nations already have a peace organization, but they do not know how to remove private opinions and use it sincerely and practically. Even our United Kingdom cannot avoid this criticism." In the afternoon, the Federation also held a conference at the Guildhall to discuss international cooperation to prevent aggression. Former Foreign Secretary Chamberlain delivered a speech. What he understood was slightly different from Lord Cecil. Cecil expressed trust in the League of Nations. Chamberlain discussed the League of Nations issue from another perspective. Chamberlain clearly advocated common international cooperation to safeguard security by stern means. Chamberlain put forward a resolution, which stated, "If a member of the League of Nations is subjected to unreasonable aggression, other member states should rise up to defend it." The meeting was enthusiastically applauded. Chamberlain continued to say that he was not unaware that some people in the United Kingdom only wanted the United Kingdom to close itself off and not have anything to do with the European continent. However, under the current situation, this isolationism is no different from "ostriches encountering danger, being frightened and burying their heads in the sand, but ultimately unable to escape the bullets of hunters. Our England has the right not to ask about foreign affairs, but the three birds of England are separated from the European continent by a water. When war breaks out in Europe, can we not be affected?" Chamberlain then said, "To safeguard British interests, there is no better way than to determine our attitude in advance. The attitude that the United Kingdom should take is to jointly prevent war. If the United Kingdom wants to seek security, Sun Li (isolation) cannot solve the problem. The effective method is still to recognize the aggressor as an enemy of all mankind." When Chamberlain said this, the meeting applauded thunderously. Chamberlain finally said, "The world organization we hope for has already sprouted since the establishment of the League of Nations. We should move forward to this goal carefully. No matter how far away the realization of our ideals is, we should not be disappointed, nor should we abandon our long-held purpose." (12th Havas Telegram)

Therefore, when the next budget案 is submitted to the House of Commons, it may include protective measures for industry. Britain Receives German Reply Explaining Increase in Military Spending; German Government Considers the Reorganization Expenses of the Army, Navy, and Air Force Extremely Justifiable 46

(London) The British Foreign Office has received Germany's reply to Britain's inquiry regarding the increase in its military spending. It is currently being considered by Foreign Secretary Simon and will probably be announced in the House of Commons within a few days. Judging from the opinions of German newspapers, the German government believes that the increase in military spending is very justifiable. Replacing single-engine aircraft with twin-engine aircraft requires enormous expenses, and the amount listed in the current air force budget is not large. As for the army, Germany plans to reorganize the National Defense Force according to a shorter conscription system, which also requires significant expenses. Germany also has the right to replace old ships with new ships. (Reuters dispatch from the 13th)

(London) After Germany increased its military spending, the British government instructed the British Ambassador to Germany, Sir Eric Phipps, to inquire with the German Foreign Office about the reasons for the increase in German military spending. The German government's reply to the British government was received here this morning. The content of the reply is being studied in detail and appears to be largely the same as the reasons given orally by the German Foreign Minister, Baron von Neurath, to the British Ambassador, namely: 1) The increase in army spending is due to the renewal required by changing over to a professional army; 2) The increase in air force spending is due to the renewal of civil aviation and the original engine

The Foreign Office will probably, as Foreign Secretary Simon promised, submit the German document to the House of Commons this afternoon. (Havas News Agency dispatch from the 12th)

Although authorities in Bucharest deny that there was a plot to harm King Carol and kidnap his girlfriend, Magda Lupescu, they have admitted today that eleven army officers have been arrested for participating in an action to overthrow the state. Famous Belgian Painting Said to Be Stolen by Germans; Intended to Undermine the Treaty of Versailles 50

Brussels: A famous painting, "Adoration of the Lamb", housed in the Church of Saint Bavo in Ghent, was stolen on April 11th. The incident is extremely bizarre, and the police are still carefully investigating. According to current speculation, the thief is probably a German secret society, and there are three reasons for this: 1) The purpose of this action is to overturn the results of the Treaty of Versailles, as the stolen painting was originally in Berlin and was later returned to Belgium under the provisions of the Treaty of Versailles. 2) The Church of Saint Bavo contains many jewels and other treasures, but the thief ignored them all. 3) Before the theft, a foreigner inquired about the church's opening and closing hours near the church. The person's accent was said to be German. (Reuters dispatch from the 13th)

Belgian Constitutional Monarchy Stable; Socialist Party Supports the New Monarch; Opposes Fascism 51

Brussels: Belgium is currently clearly expressing opposition to the Fascist Party. Since the death of former King Albert and the accession of the new monarch, Leopold III, a change in the political environment shows that the support of the Belgian Socialist Party for the new monarch is a guarantee against dictatorship and fascism. It is noteworthy that, when the former King Albert ascended the throne, the Socialist Party vehemently opposed him. However, since the succession of the new monarch, Leopold, it has been discovered that a united Socialist Party supports the continued existence of a constitutional monarchy. In addition to Socialist leader Vandervelde giving a eulogy to the former king, the Central Committee of the Socialist Party, representing the majority of the people, also voted to participate in the parliamentary address to the new monarch. The form of the address is a kind of speech after the new monarch's accession, implying the goals and hopes of the Belgian people in uniting to support the monarch and the constitution. Socialist members hope that, by participating in the address, they can consolidate constitutional government and avoid possible oppression by Fascism, as Fascism has not yet officially formed a political party. Vandervelde and other Socialist members explained that their opposition to the rule of the late King Albert was solely due to social injustice. However, Vandervelde and others also solemnly declared that Albert was truly the most democratic of monarchs and was able to implement social legislation, allowing the people to enjoy equal rights. Therefore, Socialist members are prepared to assist the constitutionally impartial heir to the throne. (National News Agency dispatch from the 13th)

The governor of Upper Austria then met with fifty of their representatives. (National News Agency dispatch from the 13th)

Difficulty in Selecting Successor After Resignation of Army Minister Lin; Contradiction Between Peaceful Diplomacy and Militarism; Prince Kan'in Returns to Capital Early for Final Decision 58

(Tokyo) Regarding the resignation of Army Minister Lin, the Army Ministry officials say that it is awaiting the decision of Chief of the General Staff Prince Kan'in after he returns to the capital. However, in reality, this is a way to delay the matter because it is difficult to select a successor internally. It is rumored that Araki's reinstatement is unlikely to materialize because Foreign Minister Hirota is currently working hard to promote peaceful diplomacy with the United States. Would it not be a contradiction if Araki's militarism were to be realized again? However, the military has expressed dissatisfaction with Army Minister Lin, believing that he cannot continue Araki's tough policies, and internally, there is actually no one who can succeed Araki. This is why it is difficult to select a successor. The financial and political circles are well aware of this fact within the military and are secretly promoting Lieutenant General Koiso Kuniaki, the former Chief of Staff of the Kwantung Army and current commander of the 5th Division, to become the Army Minister. This is because Lieutenant General Koiso has some economic knowledge and is also relatively well-informed about the world situation. However, Lieutenant General Koiso lacks the power to control the current military, so this promotion is probably difficult to achieve. At 8:50 this morning, Army Minister Lin went to his official residence. Vice Minister Yanagawa and Commander of the Military Police Qin had a long, confidential discussion with Army Minister Lin. At 10:20, he went to the Prime Minister's official residence to participate in the regular cabinet meeting. (Chinese United News Agency dispatch from the 13th)

The government is most concerned that General Araki Sadao will be reappointed as Army Minister, in which case the political parties and financial circles will inevitably launch a major movement to overthrow the cabinet. They are currently collecting information from various sources to prepare countermeasures. (Chinese United News Agency dispatch from the 13th)

Science Proves the Efficacy of the Traditional Chinese Medicine "Deer Antler" 59

Deer Antler Extract Contains a Large Amount of Male Endocrine Substance Which Can Enhance the Vitality of the Body and Has a Significant Effect on Curing Wasting Diseases

Results of Research by Russian Medical Community 60

TASS Moscow, March 13th Dispatch: For thousands of years, Chinese doctors have always used deer antler (the engorged young horns of spotted deer) as a famous medicine. The Soviet medical community has recently become quite interested in this. The Soviet Fur and Hunting Society accepted the suggestion of the famous scientist Pavlovlenko and conducted scientific tests on the medicinal properties of this substance. This work was carried out under the guidance of Pavlovlenko. Pavlovlenko has already extracted the most medicinal substance from deer antler, calling it deer antler extract. Several prominent scientists and doctors from Moscow hospitals are proving the medicinal properties of this new substance. After analysis, it is known that deer antler extract contains a large amount of male endocrine substance, which has aroused strong interest in medical theory and practice. After hospital experiments, this substance has a high degree of medicinal power, namely it can enhance the vitality of the body, the activity of the heart, and eliminate the weakness of the heart muscle, etc. It can also accelerate the healing of friction injuries and is most effective for injuries that have been infected or festered. After many patients took deer antler extract, their workload and appetite immediately increased. Those who were disabled became less indifferent and nervous. This substance is also very effective for certain gastrointestinal diseases and sclerosis. In the second half of this year, Soviet hospitals will widely apply deer antler extract. Currently, the spotted deer farm of the Coastal Province Far East Livestock Mixed Ranch has 10,000 spotted deer. Two more deer farms will be added to the area this year to raise spotted deer.

Wei Yifu Talks About the Incident of Mixing Counterfeit Postal Mail 70

(Nanjing) The mixing of counterfeit national postal mail into Beijing has caused great concern in all quarters. Further inquiries were made to the Ministry of Communications to find out what happened. According to Wei Yifu, Director of the Postal Department, after our blockade of the Northeast postal service, the counterfeit national postal service was completely managed by the Japanese. All mail from the people of the Northeast to destinations outside the counterfeit nation is handled and forwarded by the Japanese post office. If our post office receives mail from Japan and finds that it has counterfeit national stamps affixed to it, it will naturally be treated as invalid based on the principle of non-recognition. The post office will then notify the addressee and impose a penalty in accordance with the regulations on insufficient postage, requiring them to pay the penalty to redeem the letter. The policy of absolutely prohibiting our country's mail from being sent to the counterfeit nation has been consistent for two years. (Special dispatch from the 13th)

On the 13th, reporters inquired with the relevant agencies. According to officials from the Executive Yuan and the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, as of noon today, they had not yet received any reports on the matter and had already telegraphed the Yunnan Provincial Government to inquire about the truth. (Central News Agency dispatch, 13th)

(Nanjing) After the British entered Ban Hong on the Yunnan border, investigations and negotiations are underway. Suddenly, the Jian Shui County Party Department sent a telegram stating that in February, 150 to 160 armed French soldiers suddenly invaded Zhong Meng and completely occupied E’la Village, requesting national support. However, as of the afternoon of the 13th, the Ministry of Foreign Affairs had not yet received a telegram from the Yunnan Provincial Government regarding this matter. Li Pei-tian, the representative of the Yunnan Provincial Government in Beijing, is currently not in Beijing and cannot be questioned. Based on the telegram from the Jian Shui County Party Department, the Ministry of Foreign Affairs specifically telegraphed Long Yun, Chairman of Yunnan, and Wang Zhan-qi, Special Diplomatic Commissioner, urging them to quickly investigate and report back for negotiations. (Special dispatch, 13th)

(Nanjing) Regarding the Ban Hong incident, the first colonial commissioner stationed in Simao, Li Yue-gai, and the second colonial commissioner stationed in Tengchong County, Yang Yi-qian, have personally gone to Ban Hong to investigate. Li and Yang have already departed and a more detailed report is expected in Beijing in about two weeks. Yunnan Chairman Long Yun believes that the British are exploiting the pro-British minority indigenous people in Ban Hong to assist in mining, while the majority of indigenous people are resisting, leading to a war between indigenous people. Long has dispatched special commissioner Lu Guo-fan to Ban Hong to sincerely comfort the indigenous people. Lu has been a local chieftain in Yunnan for many years and is highly trusted by the indigenous people. Kunming has a special diplomatic commissioner, Wang Zhan-qi, and Yangon has a consul, Xu Cong-yun. The British also have a diplomatic commissioner stationed in Yangon and a British consul in Kunming. In addition to reporting the Ban Hong situation to the central government, the Yunnan provincial authorities have also notified Wang Zhan-qi (Nanjing) and Xu Cong-yun to negotiate with the British consuls and commissioners nearby, taking a two-pronged approach: 1. Before the Yunnan-Myanmar border is surveyed and demarcated, the British should cease mining in Ban Hong. 2. China and Britain should each send commissioners to jointly survey and demarcate the Yunnan-Myanmar border. (Special dispatch, 13th)

Shandong East Coal Mine Company Established 83

(Jinan) A production and sales cooperative for Boshan coal mines has been established. Forty articles of association have been agreed upon, named the Shandong East Coal Mine Cooperative Company. All participating mine operators will have their external sales managed by the company. Each coal mine will transport all types of coal produced to the nearest railway station and hand it over to the cooperative company for joint sale. The company's capital is set at 300,000 yuan, which will be allocated and paid according to the proportion of actual coal production of each mine. The company will be organized and established within one month after the agreement is signed and will begin operations. The company will have three supervisors, nine review committee members, a coal quality inspection committee, and a coal production review committee. It will also apply to the Department of Construction, planning to mortgage all mineral properties and mining rights of the mine operators to the banking sector for 1.5 million yuan. It is estimated that 4,000 tons of coal can be produced daily, with a levy of 5 jiao per ton, which can be repaid in about two years. Yu Wu-heng, a technical specialist from the Department of Construction, returned to Jinan on the 12th to report to Zhang Hong-lie. After review, it will be discussed with the Qingdao Municipal Government before implementation. (Central News Agency dispatch, 12th)

Japanese Troops Actively Rearranging Defenses in the War Zone 89

Japanese Garrison in Tangshan Conducts Live-Fire Exercises

Chairman of the Gubeikou Chamber of Commerce a Traitor

Beiping Correspondence: Since the counties in eastern Luan and northern Ji have been designated as war zones, Japanese and Korean ronin and general traitors, under the protection of the Japanese, have been carrying out activities on a large scale, ostensibly establishing foreign firms to secretly sell various drugs and smuggle firearms, which are resold to local bandits. As a result, general riffraff and local ruffians also have secret meeting places. Bandits are rising up, and robberies occur frequently. The Japanese army also conducts live-fire exercises from time to time to demonstrate force, causing the local people to feel uneasy and living under a cloud of terror. Not only are the traitors still trying to be active, but the Japanese army's troop movements are also particularly active.

News that the Japanese army in Gubeikou would be transferred to Zunhua and Fengrun counties had been widely circulated. However, most people still thought it was unreliable and were half-believing, half-doubting. Unexpectedly, on the morning of the 8th of this month, more than 30 Japanese soldiers took 16 heavy trucks, carrying military supplies such as guns and ammunition, and drove into Fengrun city. When asked about their intentions, they said they were visiting education and construction in the county. The Japanese soldiers also brought cameras and measuring instruments, the purpose of which is unclear. Because of the chaos of last year, local merchants and residents have become easily frightened, rumors are rife, and people are restless, with a feeling that they may not survive.

The Japanese garrison in Tangshan had always notified our Public Security Bureau in advance to inform merchants and residents of the previous exercises, so that they would not be alarmed and could maintain local order. However, during the period when the city was under serious alert due to the resolution of the labor strike in Tangshan and the search for reactionary elements, the team suddenly conducted live-fire exercises at the old shooting range in Xishan from 2:00 PM to 4:00 PM on the afternoon of the 10th without prior notice. For a time, people were in a panic, thinking that an incident had occurred. Fortunately, order was gradually restored through the maintenance of the Public Security Bureau.

Lu Tai, Zhaishang, Hangu, Zhakou and other places in Ninghe County are prosperous commercial towns and have long been areas of activity for traitors. This time, a large number of recruited poor peasants from those areas were transported to Guanjie by way of Qinhuangdao. Upon receiving the report, the Ninghe Public Security Bureau led the police and the security regiment to surround the Tianjiazhuang in the South Railway Station and arrested the traitors Zhang Yichun, Liu Mingqing, and Wang and others, a total of five people. They also seized many reactionary declarations and publications. There are still three people at large and are being hunted down.

Liu You-xun, the director of the Gubeikou Miyun Bureau, has come to Beiping from Gubeikou to visit Yin Rugeng, the administrative inspector of the Ji-Mi District, to report on government affairs. The reporter met with Liu, who said the following: Gubeikou has been relatively peaceful recently. The local population is currently about 5,000 people, mostly from other provinces. Since the Changcheng War, many people have lost their jobs and are forced by life to become traitors. Recently, in order to provide relief, the War Zone Committee has approved a spring relief program to provide 8,000 yuan to a small number of farmers to add farming tools and seeds to facilitate spring plowing. However, this money has not yet been released. The fake police at Nantianmen in Gubeikou have been allowed by the Japanese to withdraw within this month. It is still difficult to say whether this will be realized at that time. If there is no trouble from traitors in Gubeikou, it will not be difficult to restore the situation before the war in a short period of time. Zou Hong-en and Guan, the chairman and vice-chairman of the local chamber of commerce, have become traitors and have recently been re-elected. Li, who was the chairman of the chamber of commerce before the war, has succeeded them. After investigation, several places have been found where Japanese and Korean ronin are secretly selling opium and heroin. There are also local thugs who are selling drugs secretly in the name of the Japanese. The Bureau has decided to send personnel to take measures to ban them. (12th)

Chiang Orders He Chengjun to Take Responsibility for Blocking Sichuan Bandits; He Returns to Hankou from Jiangxi and Then Goes to Northern Hubei for Inspection; an Administrative Office Will Be Established in Fancheng to Facilitate Command 90

Hankou Correspondence: He Chengjun, the appeasement commissioner stationed in Hubei, was previously ordered by General Chiang to go to northern Hubei for inspection, to arrange for blocking Sichuan bandits, and was offered the position of commander-in-chief of bandit suppression in the border areas of the four provinces of Henan, Shaanxi, Sichuan, and Hubei. After He repeatedly declined, he gave up. However, He has clearly taken on the responsibility of suppressing bandits in that area. Therefore, the rumor that the appeasement office would move to northern Hubei is rampant. On the 2nd of this month, He left Hankou for Jiangxi and arrived in Nanchang on the 3rd. In eight days, he met with Chiang four times, reporting in detail on his inspection of northern Hubei and the suppression of the remaining bandits of Liu Guitang, Ma Xiyou, and Wang You. Chiang paid particular attention to preventing Sichuan bandits from fleeing to Hubei. It is said that he has commissioned He to continue to be responsible for the defense and has given instructions. After completing his official duties in Jiangxi, He and Qian Dajun, Wu Jiaxiang, and Pang Bingxun took a car to Xun on the 10th. On the 11th, He, Wu, and Pang took the Jiangxin steamer west. Qian Dajun stayed in Xun for one day on official business. After the Jiangxin steamer arrived in Hankou at 5:00 AM on the 12th, He went to the appeasement office to work and scheduled to visit Deputy Commander Zhang on the 13th, after which he will go to northern Hubei for inspection. The appeasement office has suspended its relocation and will establish an administrative office in Fancheng when necessary to facilitate command. According to He, "This time, I went to Jiangxi to report to General Chiang on the various matters of inspecting and suppressing bandits and to ask for instructions on blocking Sichuan bandits. General Chiang gave very detailed instructions. The bandit suppression military affairs in Hubei Province can be described in general terms. The remaining bandits in eastern Hubei have been surrounded and have been fleeing for too long, exhausted. We also have fresh troops joining the cooperation in suppression. It is only a matter of time before they are annihilated. There are few remaining bandits in southern Hubei, which is also easy to clear. The He bandits in western Hubei have now fled abroad, and scattered small groups are being searched and suppressed by Commander-in-Chief Xu Yuanquan. There are no traces of bandits in the central and northern Hubei regions. Local rehabilitation is still carried out according to the plan previously set by General Chiang, which needs to be implemented urgently. The cleanup and rehabilitation of the border areas of the three provinces of Henan, Hubei, and Anhui, and the command of the stationed troops, are still under the command of General Liu Zhenhua. The Xu Xiangqian bandit forces have been damaged in Sichuan and are inevitably forced to flee elsewhere, so defensive military affairs are more important. I plan to go to northern Hubei again within a few days to continue inspecting the blockhouse projects and traffic conditions in various counties in order to make proper arrangements, and then transfer to western Hubei for inspection, with the general goal of consolidating the border defense and maintaining local peace. The bandit suppression in Jiangxi has indeed made great progress. It will not be difficult to complete it within the three-month period set by General Chiang. The market in Nanchang has improved and the atmosphere is new. Because General Chiang is promoting the New Life Movement, the people have heard the style and have a vigorous spirit, which shows that this movement is indeed a need for today's Chinese society, and restoring inherent morality is enough to save the declining customs and revive the last customs. I passed by President Wang in the middle of the road when he went to Jiangxi, so I did not see him. I have also never been to Beijing or Shanghai. All kinds of external rumors are unfounded."

Liu Bandits Flee to Zhucheng; Army, Navy, and Air Force Coordinate to Encircle and Suppress 91

Jinan Correspondence: Because the Liu bandits lacked ammunition, they planned to flee to the Hongshiya seaport in Zhucheng to replenish ammunition. Yesterday, they fled to the vicinity of Lincun in the east of Zhucheng. Tonight, they were intercepted by the Wu Yuanxing regiment of the 58th Brigade of the 20th Division. The bandits suffered heavy casualties and fled in a panic to the southwest, to Gao Ge Village, and turned southeast. By the afternoon, they had fled to the vicinity of the Chaohe River and were threatening to flee to Rizhao again. The army and navy are now coordinating to block and intercept them. Central aircraft have arrived and dropped bombs today (12th), killing many bandits.

Yesterday, when the Liu bandits passed through Louzi and Zhu Supu and fled east, they were attacked from the side by the Li Zhanbiao troops of the 66th Brigade, which were chasing from the south. The bandits suffered heavy casualties. In the evening, they arrived near Lincun and still wanted to continue fleeing east. Tonight, they were intercepted by Wu Yuanxing of the 58th Brigade of the 20th Division at Xiaoshaopo. The battle was fierce in the dark. In this battle, more than 60 bandits were killed, more than 100 were captured, and more than 100 mules and horses and more than 70 guns, and one mortar were captured, with only one shell remaining. It can be seen that the bandits are lacking ammunition, so they are desperately fleeing. Now the remaining bandits are no more than 300, and the mules and horses are no more than 200. Complete annihilation is only a matter of time.

The various bandit suppression forces are now coordinating their advance. Xu Wenyao, the deputy division commander of the 29th Division, led the Li Xiangchen brigade to intercept the bandits from the southwest. The Li Zhanbiao troops of the 66th Brigade are deployed on the north side. Zhan Shutang of the 81st Brigade led the Yun Qichang brigade to take charge of the east side in Jiaoxian. The Tang Bangzhi brigade of the division is on the north side. The Third Fleet dispatched the navy to the ancient town camp at the junction of Jiaoxian and Zhucheng, and today added another ship to that location to prevent the bandits from fleeing to the seaport. Because of the large gathering of the navy, the bandits did not dare to go to Hongshiya, so they fled to Chaohe (which is only three or four li from the border of Rizhao County) and were threatening to flee to Rizhao. Two aircraft dispatched by the central government arrived in Weixian from Xuzhou in the afternoon. Today, Wang Zuwen, a senator of the provincial government, took the plane to Chaohe and dropped six 32-pound bombs, causing heavy casualties among the bandits. Because the Liu bandits fled north, the chairman of the provincial government, Han Fuju, was afraid that the spring would approach the Jiaoji Railway line, so he planned to accompany the chairman of the Jiaoji Railway Committee, Ge Guangting, on a train to inspect the line. Now that the bandits have fled south, he has decided not to leave for the time being. Therefore, Ge Guangting has already returned to Qingdao this morning. (12th)

The Political and Military Situation in Kang and Tibet (Continued) 92

The military history of the Kang region during the late Qing Dynasty involved garrison troops dispatched by the Sichuan Governor-General. These troops were rotated every three years, with salaries, equipment, and provisions supplied by Sichuan. When Zhao Erfeng came to oversee border affairs, after pacifying Xiangcheng, he proposed comprehensive border political reforms, abolishing the Governor-General's office and replacing it with border defense forces. Initially, three battalions of the Western Army, five battalions of the New Army, and one battalion of the Banner Army were established. Ultimately, it was planned to form a mixed brigade of the New Army, with military expenses totaling over 458,000 taels of silver, allocated from Sichuan's oil and sugar levies. All military supplies were obtained from Sichuan. After the Republican revolution, there were ten battalions of border defense forces and two artillery units. When Yin Changheng led the Western Expedition, he mobilized six standard units and two battalions, along with the entire Ninth and Eleventh Standards. A guard regiment was also formed with a monthly salary of 200,000 taels. In the third year of the Republic, the border garrison commander was appointed, and the remaining army troops were reorganized into the First Border Defense Command, stationed in Ba'an, with one sub-command stationed in Qamdo, and another in Jiangka, totaling eleven border defense battalions, supplemented by one battalion of the Western Expeditionary Army and two artillery units, stationed in various counties west of the Jinsha River, from Derong in the south to Shiqu in the north, and west to Qamdo's Enda. The remaining border troops were reorganized into a mixed brigade, stationed from Xiangcheng in the south to Ganzi in the north, and east to Luding, requiring a monthly border expense of 149,400 taels. In the tenth year of the Republic, Sichuan's divisions changed taels to yuan, continuing with 135,300 yuan, which was disbursed monthly by Sichuan from Military Commissioner Zhang, Liu, to Yin, and military supplies were also requested from Sichuan. The military was well-equipped, the defenses were tight, and the Kang area remained relatively peaceful. In the sixth year of the Republic, Military Commissioner Chen took office, when Sichuan declared a revolution against the Southern government, Chen sided with the Northern Warlords, leading to the cutoff of Sichuan's supplies. The garrisons in Ningyuan and Ya'an were used as substitutes. Later, the Northern government agreed to allocate 80,000 yuan per month from Sichuan's salt revenues for border expenses, which sustained them. However, since the sixth year, Tibetan bandits invaded, losing eleven counties north and south of the border. The border army commanders and their units were disarmed by the Tibetan army. The four battalions under the sub-command stationed in Ningjing were reduced to three after one battalion was disarmed. The three remaining battalions were stationed in Yanjing, Chong'an, and Ba. After the signing of the truce agreement with Tibet in the seventh year, the army brigade was gradually withdrawn to Ya'an, leaving only a battalion of reorganized border troops in Ba'an and Yanjing, and a battalion divided between Ganzi and Zhanhua. The rest were transferred to the Ya'an River area, leaving the border defenses empty and bandits rampant. County officials in Derong and Xiangcheng were repeatedly killed and driven out, and their camp guns were seized. Local thugs became increasingly lawless, and the authority of the government declined, leading to the disintegration of border administration. After Military Commissioner Liu's land reclamation in Kang, the Kang area was still guarded by the original garrison troops, without any reorganization, making it impossible to speak of any military administration. After this army took over Kang, it reorganized the border army into the 14th Brigade and sent the 10th Brigade to Luding to exert control. Later, due to the Sichuan war, the 10th Brigade was transferred internally, leaving only the 14th Brigade as the garrison. Subsequently, the Sichuan-Kang Border Defense Army was established, reorganizing the 10th Brigade into the 1st Brigade, temporarily stationed in Qionglai and Ya'an for training, and reorganizing the 14th Brigade into the 2nd Brigade, with Regiment Commander Ma Sheng promoted to brigade commander. In the 19th year, the 39th Regiment of the 1st Brigade was transferred from Da Jin Temple to Kang for support, stationed in the Daofu-Luhuo area. In the 21st year, during the Tibetan campaign, the 53rd Regiment of the 1st Brigade and the 46th and 48th Regiments of the Ningyuan Defense Army were mobilized to assist in the battle. That winter, the Sichuan war broke out, and the 53rd Regiment was transferred internally. The 11th Brigade was stationed in Kang for garrison duty, merging into one regiment, the 48th Regiment. The total number of troops garrisoning Kang was the 39th Regiment, the 40th Regiment, and the 42nd Regiment, with each battalion supplemented by special forces companies, and a newly formed cavalry regiment, stationed on the east bank of the Jinsha River, confronting the Kang army. The second line of defense in the north, south, and central routes was also continuously reinforced with battalions stationed to provide support. Only a special duty company and two mountain artillery batteries remained in Luding. It was discovered that the Kang army's salaries, provisions, and military supplies all depended on the army headquarters' allocations. However, since the army retreated to Ya'an last year, the border expenses have become unsustainable, and even the strategic rice production area of Mingshan and Hongya Counties was lost, resulting in the Kang army's current situation of extreme financial and supply shortages.

Changes in Tibetan Affairs

Kang and Tibet are neighbors. Governing Kang without first addressing Tibetan affairs will lead to external threats and hinder internal administration. Moreover, Kang and Tibet are of the same ethnicity. If Tibetan affairs are unsettled, Kang affairs will inevitably be affected. Since the Republican revolution, the army mutiny greatly alienated the Tibetan people, leading to daily resistance and separation to this day. The divide between Han and Tibetan people has not been resolved and is, in fact, growing. It was found that in the first year of the Republic, when Lian Zhong and the Dalai Lama fell out, the stationed troops were forced to disarm by the Tibetans. At that time, Yuan Shikai coveted the country's leadership, and the British deliberately stirred up trouble, using Tibet as a bargaining chip, recognizing the Republic in exchange. Therefore, a laissez-faire policy was adopted towards Tibetan affairs. After Lian Yu left Tibet, he merely procrastinated and temporarily appointed Lu Xingqi as the acting chief of the Tibetan Affairs Office. Lu lacked prestige and was originally a low-level merchant. His sudden appointment to a high-ranking position was seen as an insult by the Dalai Lama, who perceived that the Han people had no intention of governing Tibet. Consequently, he severed communications with the central government, and the British took the opportunity to instigate the Tibetans to advocate for autonomy, making the Tibetan situation untenable. Yin Changheng's Western Expedition had an imposing military presence. At that time, Sichuan's financial resources were sufficient to supply his military needs. If Yuan Shikai had not sought personal gain and been timid in listening to their westward advancement, it would not have been difficult to restore the old order. However, he ordered the cessation of advancement and designated Qamdo Enda as the stopping point, preventing the Han army from crossing the Lancang River. The Tibetan people relied on Britain as their protector and became hostile to the Han people. In the sixth year, a minor dispute over grass cutting instigated Tibetan soldiers to take advantage of the situation to invade. Coinciding with the national division between the north and south, Military Commissioner Chen raised the Northern banner and focused on Sichuan, neglecting border defense, allowing the Tibetans to seize eleven counties. The signing of the Rongbaqia truce terms allowed the Tibetans to fulfill their ambition. For more than ten years, China was preoccupied with internal conflicts and did not consider Tibet. The Tibetan people have occupied the land for a long time, considering it their own. The Panchen Lama, due to his pro-Han stance, was forced into exile by the Dalai Lama. China could neither stabilize Tibet through military force nor reconcile the Dalai Lama and Panchen Lama's affairs. Instead, it ceremoniously sent the Panchen Lama back to Tibet, singing high praises, further arousing Tibetan suspicion, and worsening Han-Tibetan relations. In the nineteenth year, the Da Jin dispute was not a major issue. The Tibetan side initially intended not to intervene, with some saying that Han officials should handle it themselves. However, ignorant individuals fabricated claims that the Kang army intended to use this opportunity to escort the Panchen Lama back to Tibet. Da Jin then instigated the Dalai Lama to formally assign troops to engage in warfare with the Han people, thereby escalating the situation. Following the Da Jin incident, the central government naively believed the Dalai Lama's claims of peace, prohibiting the Kang army from advancing militarily and demanding that the central government send personnel to mediate and both sides to withdraw their troops and cease fire. At that time, the Tibetan army was west of Da Jin, and our army was east of Baili. The Tibetan army withdrew to its original defense, only a station away. The central government's special envoy for mediation, Tang Keshan, had already arrived in Chongqing. However, Da Jin instigated the Tibetan army to launch a sneak attack while Tang's troops were complying with orders to withdraw and defend, seizing Ganzi and advancing to Zhuwo in Luhuo, and also dispatching troops to seize Zhanhua, which had not been garrisoned by Kang troops. As a result, Tang's delegation proposed that the Tibetan side first comply with the Dalai Lama's telegram ordering the withdrawal of troops from Ganzi and Zhanhua before starting negotiations. The Tibetan side claimed that it was not fulfilling the Dalai Lama's orders, and subsequently, the Dalai Lama formally requested the National Government to subordinate Ganzi and Zhanhua to the Tibetan government. Although the central government refuted this, the Tibetan side ignored it. Tang Kesan's negotiations were ineffective, and he planned to use military force as a backing, requesting the central government to provide the Kang army with funds and equipment to recover the lost territory before resuming negotiations, and also ordering the Qinghai army to assist. The National Government did not provide a concrete response to this proposal for several months. The Dongzhou Difficulty arose, and the Mongolian and Tibetan Affairs Commission telegraphed Tang to conclude the matter with expediency. Consequently, the Guntuo truce agreement was hastily signed, allowing Tibetan troops to be stationed in Ganzi and Zhanhua. General Liu Wenhui and the Sichuan people strongly opposed this agreement, which was never signed. Tang was then ordered to return to the capital, and the central government telegraphed General Liu Wenhui, granting him full authority over Tibetan affairs. Thus, this army decided to recover the lost territory and wage war against Tibet. The Kang army set April 28th of the 21st year as the date to begin the attack. Tibet launched an attack on the Kang army on the first day. The Kang army divided its command into north and south routes, taking the opportunity to recapture Ganzi and Zhanhua. Tibet greatly reinforced its troops. The Kang army reorganized into five detachments, launching an offensive in the north, south, and central routes, engaging in fierce battles with the Tibetan army between Da Jin and Baili. The Tibetan army could not withstand the attack, and Da Jin was captured. The victory was exploited to advance directly to the east bank of the Jinsha River, successively recovering the four counties of Deyu, Baiyu, Dengke, and Shiqu. A joint attack on Qamdo with the Qinghai army was planned. However, the outbreak of the Sichuan War made it necessary to accept the Tibetan side's request and establish the Gangtuo truce terms.

The Tibetan Army's Strength, Organization, and Deployment

The entire Tibetan army consists of eleven Dabens (a Daben is equivalent to a regiment). During the fighting last year, there were a total of nine Dabens. After the establishment of the Gangtuo truce terms, some were recalled to Central Tibet. After the Qinghai-Tibet agreement was established, troops were dispatched to the Qanglei area, and transferred to Bomi, Shuo Luo Border, Riwuqê, Gongjue, Zhalie, and Jiangka. Militiamen were assigned to the Dabens. According to detailed investigations, the Tibetan side deployed nine Dabens in the north and south routes, with two Dabens in the south route and seven Dabens in the north route. In addition to the 500 troops in the headquarters, each Daben is attached with special forces and militia. Based on the Tibetan army's deployment and recent movements, it is speculated that their talk of peace is a tactic, while their repeated dispatch of personnel to Ya'an (recently, the Tibetan side has repeatedly sent official letters to Ya'an to visit Liu Wenhui, and this reporter encountered two of them at Da Xiangling on the way to Kang) suggests an intent to scout out Sichuan's situation and the Kang army's internal affairs. After these personnel return to Qamdo, it is feared that intense battles will break out.

Dredging of the Songjiang Municipal River Commences 93

Preparations for dredging the Songjiang city river have been underway for more than three months. Various plans have been submitted to and approved by the Construction Department, which has also approved the Tai Chang Quarry's construction department to contract the entire project. The official subsidy is 28,000 yuan, and sufficient funds have been raised for the project. Local donations have been collected from two months' worth of rents. The county government has recently announced the dredging procedures, which will begin from the Xinhua Yang Bridge to the east, west to the Qianjing Bridge at the Dongmenkou, and end at the Xizhalu outside the Kuatang Bridge. The branch rivers will be dredged from the Heiqiao to the Pingqiao, and the Hezhang Bridge from the Nanmen to the south of the Pingqiao. The contractor will immediately begin damming the water. The county government has announced that vessels within the affected sections must relocate to facilitate the project.

The dispute over the bankruptcy debts of Songjiang Bank has not yet concluded. The lawsuit filed by credit representatives Bai Guanlan and others is undergoing final arguments in the High Court's appellate review, with a scheduled date for pronouncement. Changshu Bank Employee Commits Suicide by Poisoning 99

Li Kaixi, a 22-year-old employee of the accounting department of the Bank of China in this county, recently transferred from Nanjing to Changshu, just 20 days ago. He was known to be quite honest. On the 11th, he suddenly received a telegram from home and became gloomy and did not eat dinner. Around 9:00 PM, he was heard snoring loudly while sleeping. However, he did not get up until 10:00 AM the next morning. Colleagues went upstairs to wake him up as it was office hours, but found him cold and barely breathing. They immediately reported to Bank Manager Hao Shebo, who urgently sent him to Jishan Hospital in the North Gate for treatment. Upon examination, there was no suspicious evidence or suicide note on his bedside. Only an empty bottle of Lysol disinfectant was found on the table, indicating that he had taken poison. However, after being sent to the hospital, he died at 1:00 PM due to the severity of the poisoning, despite efforts to save him. The bank urgently telegraphed his family in Zhenjiang to come to Changshu to handle the funeral.

Local News

National Economic Commission Decides to Ship American Loaned Flour to Northwest, Road Construction in Northwest Needs Many Workers and Enormous Expenditure, National Flour Has No Market There, So Conflict Can Be Avoided 107

Shenshi News Agency reports that among the cotton and wheat loans signed by Song Ziwen in the United States, 10 million yuan was for wheat loans. Later, the US Financial Relief Bureau, accepting the requests of the American flour manufacturers, negotiated with our government to ship $4 million gold worth of flour, totaling about 300,000 tons or 6 million small bags, out of the 10 million yuan in wheat loans. The National Economic Commission, considering that domestic flour has no market, has decided to ship it to the Northwest for the consumption of road construction workers. Shenshi News Agency reporters have investigated the situation as follows:

To Be Used as Food for Northwest Road Construction Workers 108

Due to frequent years of famine, poor wheat harvests, and reliance on foreign aid, the country relies on foreign aid for wheat. As for flour, the domestic production is huge. Shanghai alone can produce more than 100,000 bags per day. Imports of foreign flour will clearly conflict with domestic production. The National Economic Commission's Standing Committee, Song Ziwen, Minister of Finance Kong Xiangxi, and Rong Jingjing and other flour manufacturers in Shanghai have repeatedly consulted and decided to ship all the American loaned flour to the Northwest for consumption by road construction workers. The Northwest is currently carrying out large-scale road construction projects such as the Xilan Highway and the Xihan Highway, which require thousands of workers every day and consume a large amount of flour. Shanghai flour mills have traditionally lacked a market in the Northwest, so using American flour can avoid conflict. This is a win-win situation.

Shipping Costs and Vessels Have Been Negotiated 109

The first batch of American flour arrived in Shanghai on February 23, totaling 6,000 bags, which were sold out locally. There have been no continued shipments since. Now that the Economic Commission has decided to use it as road construction food for workers in the Northwest, it will no longer be sold in Shanghai in the future to avoid conflicts with the sales of Shanghai factories. It is planned that after June, all the flour will be entrusted to the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company for transport from the United States to Haizhou Laoyao for unloading, then transferred to the Longhai Railway for westward transportation and delivered to the Xi'an Economic Commission Office for verification and distribution to each road project. According to a certain official of the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company, the American loaned cotton and wheat will depart from Portland and Seattle. The ships needed have been negotiated by Section Chief He Molin in the United States. The shipping cost from the United States to China will be about US$2.5 per ton, saving about US$1 per ton compared to direct transportation by other foreign ships.

Kong Xiangxi and Rogers Arrived in Shanghai Together Yesterday Morning, Kong's Tea Party Rescheduled for Today, Zhang Gongquan and Others Gave a Banquet for Rogers Last Night 110

Minister of Finance Kong Xiangxi, accompanied by Professor Rogers, a silver expert dispatched by US President Roosevelt to investigate China, arrived in Shanghai together at 7:30 yesterday morning on the night train.
