Spain National Day - Expatriates Celebrate Today 111

The Spanish constitution has been in a state of flux for seven years. Since the municipal elections of April 12, 1931, Spanish public opinion has clearly favored the restoration of the republic. After the election results were announced, the monarch abdicated, and the republic was declared two days later. The change of government occurred without bloodshed. Once the parliament convened, a new constitution was promulgated, and Niceto Alcalá-Zamora assumed the presidency. President Alcalá-Zamora was highly respected and enjoyed popular support. Coming from a distinguished family, Alcalá-Zamora made significant contributions to Spanish politics. He studied diligently under his father's tutelage and graduated from the University of Granada at the age of seventeen with a law degree and a doctorate. He initially served as a government judge and held ministerial positions in several cabinets. However, he retired from public life after General Primo de Rivera established a dictatorship, as he firmly believed in liberalism and was loyal to the nation, refusing to be intimidated by power. He later became a founding member of the revolution. On April 13, 1930, he issued a rallying cry in Valencia, becoming a pioneer of the republic and a key figure in the shift of public sentiment. In this public statement, Alcalá-Zamora declared that a republican government was the only way to stabilize the Spanish political situation. On December 11, 1931, amidst enthusiastic cheers, Alcalá-Zamora swore to uphold the constitution and assumed the presidency, diligently serving the country to this day. The foundation of the Spanish Republic has been stabilized, and his contributions have been significant. The Spanish people have been able to promote and enhance it, making it a glorious event in history, worthy of being remembered. The Spanish people have therefore designated April 14th as their National Day. The Spanish Consul-General in Shanghai has scheduled a commemorative event from 11:00 AM to 12:00 PM at the Cathay Hotel, inviting government officials, local authorities, and foreign diplomats to participate in the grand occasion. Spanish expatriates will hold a celebration from 12:30 PM to 1:30 PM at the Spanish Consulate-General at No. 1205 Jing'an Temple Road.

French International Trade Association Petitions for Promotion of Sino-French Trade - Chinese International Trade Association Submits its Views 112

According to the Central News Agency, the Chinese International Trade Association previously received a letter from the National Federation of Chambers of Commerce, which included a petition form from the Paris International Trade Association for promoting Sino-French trade, as well as a request for the appointment of two Chinese representatives to participate in various events. The association was asked to submit its views. Yesterday, the association sent a reply to the National Federation of Chambers of Commerce, stating that it had received a letter forwarded by the International Trade Bureau, based on an order from the Ministry of Industry and Commerce, which in turn was based on a letter from the Ministry of Foreign Affairs. According to a report from the Consulate General in Paris, the Vice-President of the Paris International Trade Association sent a petition form to promote Sino-French trade and requested the appointment of two Chinese representatives to participate in various events, with the intention of appointing Lu Qinzhai and Ma Shoubai as representatives. The matter was submitted to the Ministry for review and instructed the Bureau to inform the International Trade Association and relevant organizations, and to inquire whether there were any volunteers to send representatives to participate in the association, and whether they agreed with the Consulate General's proposal to appoint Lu Qinzhai and Ma Shoubai, as well as to deliberate on the committee's petition and provide a detailed response. The letter was forwarded to the association, which in turn forwarded it to this association for review. The association notes that the Paris International Trade Association held a meeting last year, and the International Trade Bureau's letter was approved by the Ministry of Industry and Commerce to send representatives. However, due to the proximity of the meeting, the association was unable to send personnel and replied to the International Trade Bureau, submitting a report on file. This time, the association sent a petition form and reiterated its request for the appointment of representatives. The Consul General in Paris proposed to appoint Lu and Ma as representatives, and the Ministry ordered a review. This association has not received a letter from the International Trade Bureau informing it of this matter. Now, with the letter from your association forwarding the previous cause, this association expresses its strong agreement with the Paris Consul General's proposal to appoint Lu and Ma as representatives to participate in the association. As for the various requests mentioned in the petition form of the Paris International Trade Association, this association has carefully considered them and presents its opinions as follows: Regarding the association's request to reduce the tax rates on French specialty industrial products such as woolen yarn, woolen fabrics, cloth, printed fabrics, silk fabrics, rayon fabrics, perfumes, cosmetics, lace, champagne, high-quality brandy, and cheese, etc., it should be noted that tariffs are divided into fiscal tariffs and protective tariffs. Fiscal tariffs are aimed at enriching the national treasury, and their tax rates are naturally limited. Protective tariffs, on the other hand, are aimed at protecting domestic industries and resisting foreign competition, and their tax rates are naturally different from fiscal tariffs. However, the interests of consumers should also be taken into account, and the rates should not exceed what is necessary. Furthermore, excessively high tax rates will inevitably lead to smuggling, and the resulting increase in administrative expenses may outweigh the benefits. Since China's achievement of tariff autonomy, the tax rates on woolen yarn, woolen fabrics, cloth, silk fabrics, rayon fabrics, perfumes, cosmetics, and cheese have indeed increased significantly compared to the old tax rates. However, these goods either have luxury characteristics or, although not luxury goods, are not French products. Due to the most-favored-nation clause in China's tariff treaties, if the tax rates on these French imports are reduced, then similar products from other countries will also benefit equally, which may not be feasible at present. This association believes that maintaining the current tax rates for a considerable period is still a way to balance the interests of both parties. Regarding the association's request to separately stipulate the tax rates for raw silk and rayon, and to avoid levying excessively high tax rates on rayon as it is a daily necessity, it should be noted that rayon is a raw material for textiles, and China does not currently produce it. Therefore, its tax rate cannot be compared with that of natural silk and should be levied at a lower rate. In the past, rayon was subject to an ad valorem tax of 5%, which was increased to 10% in 1929. Calculated at the prices at the time, this amounted to slightly more than 10 taels per dan. In the 1931 tariff, it was changed to a specific duty of 58 gold units per dan. Since August 1932, it has been further increased to 73 gold units per dan, which is equivalent to more than 80% ad valorem. The tax rate cannot be said to be low. India's import tax on rayon is only 25% ad valorem, and Japan's is 101 yuan per 100 catties, both of which are lower than China's. Since the successive tax increases, the import volume of rayon has been declining year by year, and smuggling is rampant, which is detrimental to legitimate merchants. This association believes that reducing the import tax on rayon is feasible from the perspective of developing domestic industries and expanding the national treasury. This request seems to be acceptable. Regarding the association's request to protect trademark rights and the original names of various commodities, such as champagne, brandy, and cheese, etc., Article 6 of China's Trademark Law stipulates that "Foreign nationals who wish to exclusively use their trademarks in accordance with treaties on mutual protection of trademarks shall apply for registration in accordance with this law." Therefore, French imported goods that have been registered can be protected by law, which is not a problem. Regarding the association's request to reduce the taxes on various important Chinese exports, it should be noted that taxing export goods will increase the cost of domestic production and reduce their competitiveness in the international market. In recent times, countries, except for a few special monopoly products, not only exempt taxes on general goods but also provide subsidies. China's international trade has long been in a state of deficit. In recent years, due to the loss of some trade in the three northeastern provinces and the impact of the global economic recession and the increase in tariff barriers in various countries, the deficit has become even more severe. In 1932, it reached more than 500 million yuan, and in 1933, it reached more than 700 million yuan. The future is dangerous and indescribable. Export taxes should be abolished as soon as possible as a remedial measure. Furthermore, international trade aims at mutual exchange, and tariffs should be based on the principle of reciprocity to benefit both parties. If France asks China to reduce import taxes, the association's goods will also be given corresponding preferential treatment. According to the Sino-French tariff treaty, the Chinese goods that enjoy the lowest tax rates include pure silk fabrics, pure silk scarves, pure silk crepe, pure silk nets, pure silk lace, pepper, chili, cinnamon, nutmeg with shell, cloves, and tea. However, major export goods to France, such as eggs and egg products, peanuts, raw silk, silkworm cocoons, straw hat frames, pig intestines, pig bristles, tung oil, cowhide, and antimony, have not been explicitly included in the lowest tax rates, which hinders the promotion of Sino-French trade. This association hopes that the association understands this situation and also suggests to the French government that the above goods be allowed to enjoy the lowest tax rates, which will greatly benefit the progress of trade between the two countries. This association's opinion is as such, and a corresponding letter is sent for your consideration.

Joint Meeting of the British Chamber of Commerce and the Shanghai Branch of the China Association Held the Day Before Yesterday 113

According to the North-China Daily News, the British Chamber of Commerce in Shanghai and the Shanghai branch of the China Association held a joint annual meeting yesterday (the 12th) at the Shanghai Club. Speakers included Marshall, the President of the Chamber of Commerce, Brenan, the British Consul-General in Shanghai, and Peel, the Commercial Counselor of the British Legation. Marshall first delivered a speech, generally outlining the following points:

(I) China's Trade. At last year's annual meeting, it was mentioned that 1932 was one of the worst years in the history of Chinese trade, and 1933 saw further decline. This year, apart from the Fujian Incident, the Jiangxi Rebellion, and minor disturbances in the north, China did not experience any major internal wars or unrest that would affect commerce in a vast area. Although Chinese trade was hampered by restrictive taxes and unstable conditions, the main reason for the decline in trade was the situation outside China.

(II) Internal Disorder. Although the Fujian Incident never threatened the central government, the government spent a great deal of military expenditure as a result. Otherwise, this money could have been used for construction projects. Military operations to suppress the communists in Jiangxi Province and elsewhere still require a large army, but the government is fully aware of the economic nature of the problem. Therefore, it is now working hard to revive the countryside. The government's work is not easy and will take time to succeed. However, unless the economic conditions of those working in rural areas are improved, appropriate rural systems are established, and all kinds of exorbitant taxes are abolished, communism cannot be eradicated, and troublemakers will still have fertile ground to sow destructive ideas. The rural development and New Life Movement are spreading rapidly throughout the country. If the enthusiasm of the general public can remain unchanged for a long time, it will have a significant impact on the lives of the people and will directly benefit the economic situation. If China can rebuild its foundations according to the principles set by those who promote the New Life Movement and succeed, then there is no need to worry about the upper structure.

(III) Purchasing Power. The decline in trade in 1933 was largely due to the result of the world's economic misfortunes, which reduced purchasing power, and the adoption of artificial methods by many countries to seek national prosperity. Here, the total value of China's import and export trade in 1933 is compared with that of 1932 (excluding the three northeastern provinces). In 1933, it decreased by 136 million yuan, or about 15%. Tax revenue, however, increased by 46 million yuan due to increased tariffs. The new tariff regulations were implemented in 1933, many of which were too high, causing great damage to import trade. However, they can be revised in a scientific way so that trade and tax revenue are not harmed. The current tariffs are both hindering legitimate trade and making it profitable to smuggle certain kinds of goods. Therefore, both legitimate traders and tax revenue are suffering losses.

(IV) Factories. Although the increase in factories equipped with electric machinery to manufacture various goods for domestic consumption was not significant this year, it is still progressing step by step. Although the output of many factories is currently relatively small, its movement is worthy of attention. Although the yarn factories' business is languishing, new factories are still being opened, but more in the outer provinces. In the future, with the convenience of transportation, this kind of development will inevitably spread more widely. The bleaching and dyeing industry is also developing, and several of the newest factories are currently under construction. In addition, the woolen fabric industry, which China has never paid attention to, is now seeing an increase in demand due to the high taxes on wool materials. Therefore, some people have ordered woolen fabric weaving machines, and in the future, there will inevitably be many people who will engage in this industry. The electric power equipment for lighting and industrial use is now receiving great attention. When the situation is stable in the future, or when natural disasters are eliminated, the national demand will inevitably increase greatly.

(V) Railways, Highways, and Telegraphs. The construction of the Guangdong-Hankou Railway, using funds from the British return of the Boxer Indemnity, has begun and is planned to be 220 miles long. It can be completed in about three years. There is also an important railway currently under construction by the Zhejiang Provincial authorities, namely the Hangzhou-Jiangshan Railway. It has now been extended to Yushan and will eventually connect with the Guangdong-Hankou Railway via Pingxiang. The construction of highways in various provinces is also actively underway. The Shanghai-Nanjing Highway will be completed this summer. Once the main roads are completed, the construction of branch roads can make the development of the Jiangsu Province industry easier and more progressive. Based on the current rate of progress, the major cities will soon be connected by a highway network, which will greatly benefit the national political, economic, and social life. In addition, it will facilitate transportation and the transport of goods. The communication of telephone and telegraph has also made progress through the expansion of wireless and landlines. At the beginning of this year, the Zhenru Marconi Radio Station was able to directly communicate with London via wireless telegraph. Soon, it will be possible to establish commercial telephone communication with London. The progress of domestic transportation will greatly help commerce.

(VI) Siberian Mail. Commerce relies heavily on prompt information. Now, due to political difficulties, mail to and from Central Europe cannot use the fastest route via Dalian, which causes delays in delivery, greatly harming and inconveniencing merchants. It is hoped that this kind of commercial obstacle can be eliminated as soon as possible.

(VII) Changing Tael to Yuan. The government and business community now use silver dollars in general. If the composition and weight of the silver dollars remain unchanged for a long time, then this move will be very beneficial to commerce. The silver coins minted by the Central Mint have been chemically tested from time to time, and no differences have been found in their weight and composition.

(VIII) Silver Price Fluctuations. The price of silver is artificially raised. If other goods do not rise at the same time, then it cannot have any lasting beneficial effect, even in silver-producing countries. China is a silver-using country. Any artificial method to raise the price of silver will hinder its export trade and increase the already large trade surplus, which will have harmful results on trade and commerce. Therefore, it is hoped that the current recommendations strongly advocated by foreign countries can be cancelled.

(IX) New Weights and Measures System. After the customs adopted the new system, the difficulties it encountered were not as severe as initially expected. Although the conversion is very troublesome and time-consuming, it is inevitable at the beginning of the reform.

(X) Sino-Foreign Lawsuits. When merchants encounter commercial disputes, they are still unwilling to sue in local courts and prefer to mediate outside the courts. However, it is heard that as a result of negotiations, matters concerning appeals and delays have been revised. As a result, there has been progress in civil law administration, and unwarranted appeals are gradually decreasing. However, there are still many areas that need to be reformed.

(XI) Commodity Labeling. The implementation period of the regulations on labeling commodities with the country of origin has been extended from August 1, 1933 to July 1, 1934. However, the recently formulated regulations still have many technical obstacles and need to be revised in various ways before implementation.

(XII) Foreign Investment in China. Although the Chinese authorities often draw foreigners' attention to investment opportunities in China, it seems difficult to attract foreign capital if China continues to discriminate against the products of factories that are entirely or partially managed by foreigners. In the past, China only encouraged industrialists and never cared about the needs and well-being of farmers and rural workers. Now, it is known that it is engaged in rural development. It is hoped that in the future, equal importance will be attached to both agriculture and industry, without any discrimination. If China's industry continues to ignore agriculture, it will never succeed. Although China's trade and commerce declined this year, it has made genuine progress in various aspects, especially the material development of various provinces and cities. The Chinese authorities are now working hard to improve the lives of their citizens, which will have a beneficial reaction and improve the trade situation. After Marshall finished speaking, he reported on the work done by the Chamber of Commerce in the past year, followed by the British Consul-General.

Brenan's Speech 114

Briefly stated that the British government's policy towards China, in a nutshell, is to assist China's development and maintain an effective and stable government in accordance with the treaty. The British government has this purpose in mind and has stated that it is willing to follow the wishes and aspirations of the Chinese as far as possible, while paying due attention to the existing interests of the British. Recently, British Ambassador Sir Knatchbull-Hugessen told us at a banquet that the British government's policy has not changed. What we are most concerned about is trade between China and Britain. Our main objective is the Chinese market. In the future, when the provinces return to a state of tranquility, this market will inevitably expand indefinitely, and the only force that can give us this situation is a strong Chinese government. Therefore, we sympathize with the Chinese people's desire for good governance and to be governed by themselves. As for the internal unrest in China, we should not be too impatient or exaggerate it. It should be known that China's territory is as wide as Europe, and Europe also has a lot of unrest today. Then Marshall thanked Brenan and invited.

Peel to Speak 115

Peel stood up and delivered a speech, briefly stating that the chairman had just mentioned the situation of China's import and export trade and asked you to pay attention to its decline. It was found that it fell by no less than 33% in 1931 and 1932, and fell by another 15% in 1933. In the first two months of this year, it continued to fall by 20%. One of the major weaknesses of Chinese trade is that the number of exports is less than half of the number of imports. I don't know what method will be used to make up for it. Although overseas Chinese remit huge sums of money every year, I am afraid that it is less than 25 million pounds per year. If so, there are still 25 million pounds that cannot be offset. China's import trade is now greatly affected by domestic products. This can be proved by the cotton textile industry. The import of raw cotton was 250,000 dan in 1912 and has increased to 3.75 million dan in 1932, all for the use of domestic factories to make yarn and weave cloth. In these twenty years, cotton yarn has fallen from 2.5 million dan to 96,000 dan, and the rest has been replaced by domestic products. Cotton fabrics have been reduced from 2 million dan to 200,000 dan, a reduction of 60% in the past four or five years. This is indeed extremely unwelcome by British merchants, but the number of British cotton goods imported into China today is still increasing compared to the past ten years. The United Kingdom is now the second largest supplier of cotton goods needed by China. If we talk about the entire British Empire, it is the largest supplier, accounting for 30% of the total imports. The number of China's exports to the United Kingdom has also increased compared to the past ten years. The United Kingdom is the largest buyer of Chinese eggs, and the number of eggs imported into the United Kingdom is the first on the list. It has defeated Denmark. The eggs exported to the United Kingdom last year were worth more than 2.5 million pounds. The increase in British trade with China is not due to China's boycott of Japanese goods, but to the superior competitiveness of the United Kingdom. Peel continued to say that China has a vast territory, a large population, and the people are hardworking and able to endure hardship. In the future, when the local area is stable and the industry is guided by capable people, it will definitely be able to quickly occupy a position among the major countries in the world. Then he reported on the accounts, which were approved by the audience, and new directors were elected, and all the old directors were re-elected. Then the meeting of the China Association was opened. The only speaker was President Hu Dehai, who generally discussed various matters and mentioned the political situation in China.

Mystery of the Missing Central Aviation Aircraft

Ten Aircraft Sent Out Yesterday Morning to Investigate and Discover the Aircraft's Flight Direction - Jin Tangshan Island Residents Reported Seeing It Fly West at 9:00 AM That Day - According to General Speculation, the Aircraft Has Not Crashed and There Must Be Other Reasons - A Large Number of Aircraft Will Continue to Be Dispatched Today to Investigate the Whereabouts Based on Clues - The Stranded Sikorsky Aircraft Was Damaged by Waves and Will Be Towed Back by a Ship 122

According to Shenshi News Agency, the Central Aviation Corporation's No. 16 Sikorsky aircraft has been missing for four days. Yesterday, starting from the morning, all parties continued to dispatch ten aircraft to search. By 5:30 PM, the aircraft had returned one after another, but there were still no results. Only a very noteworthy clue was discovered. According to one of the pilots dispatched, Norris, he reported to the company at 3:30 PM after returning that he had landed on Jin Tangshan Island, which is about twenty miles away from Yuxingnao. According to the villagers there, the aircraft had flown over the island on Tuesday morning, but it was flying westward. According to the company's report, aircraft will be dispatched directly to the Zhejiang-Jiangxi border and the Poyang Lake area this morning to investigate. At the same time, suspicious points have also been discovered regarding a passenger on the aircraft. The Shenshi News Agency reporter will record the details as follows:

Ten Aircraft Dispatched for Search Along the Route 123

Yesterday, a total of ten aircraft were dispatched to search for the missing aircraft, including two China Aviation Corporation Lockheed aircraft, with Allison and Norris each accompanied by a radio operator, departing at 6:10 AM. Two Eurasia Junkers aircraft departed at 10:30 AM. Four aircraft dispatched by the Hangzhou Aviation School departed from Hangzhou at 11:00 AM. A Hawker Condor aircraft departed at 8:00 AM. White of the Far East Company, accompanied by his wife, departed in their aircraft at 8:00 AM, searching separately along the coast and land. After 2:00 PM, the aircraft returned one after another. Despite the day-long efforts of all the aircraft, the whereabouts of Aircraft No. 16 remained undiscovered.

Pilot Discovers Whereabouts of Missing Aircraft 124

According to pilot Norris, who departed at the same time yesterday, after returning at 3:30 PM, he reported to the company that the aircraft had flown to Kington Island (twenty miles away from Voloano Island) and landed there. (According to that location, it was the place from where the aircraft telegraphed its return at 8:30 AM on the day of the disappearance). Searching everywhere, the islanders reported that the missing aircraft had flown over the island at 9:00 AM on Tuesday morning, heading west. All the people on the island witnessed this. According to the company and experts, based on the report, they speculated that the aircraft had not crashed and that there must be other reasons. The aircraft had telegraphed from Voloano Island at 8:30 AM that it was returning, yet at 9:00 AM it was still flying west of the island. This clearly indicated that it had not returned and had not crashed, but that there was some other unfathomable reason.

Company Announces Suspicious Passenger 125

Although some oil slicks were found in the sea near Zhoushan Island as a result of the day-long search yesterday, there was still no more reliable discovery, making it difficult to determine that the aircraft had crashed into the water. The aircraft carried two rubber inflatable rafts on its wings, and if the aircraft had sunk, the rafts would definitely have floated to the surface. According to the company's announcement yesterday, the missing aircraft's passenger has been found to be highly suspicious. The passenger was named (Yuemura) and his destination was Fuzhou. When he purchased the ticket from the company, he spoke Japanese, so the company staff all regarded him as Japanese. However, according to the Japanese Consulate, there is no such Japanese person in Shanghai. Moreover, an hour after the passenger boarded the aircraft, two Chinese people suddenly came to the company, requesting the company to send a wireless message to the passenger on the aircraft. The message was in English, and the gist of it was to tell the passenger that after arriving in Fuzhou, he must quickly take a ship to another place, but the destination was not specified. The company refused according to regulations, and the two men left in disappointment. After the news of the aircraft's disappearance spread, neither the passenger's relatives nor the two Chinese people came to the company to inquire about it. According to various speculations, the passenger is indeed highly suspicious. The company has telegraphed the government and the Ministry of Communications with all the suspicious clues discovered yesterday.

Aircraft Dispatched Today to Search Westward 126

After receiving Norris's report yesterday, the company firmly believes that most of the aircraft has not crashed, but has strayed elsewhere due to some reason. Therefore, they will dispatch more aircraft today to search for it on various islands, and dispatch other aircraft to search westward, hoping to find traces in the Poyang Lake area on the border of Jiangxi and Zhejiang. It is also possible that the aircraft carried enough gasoline for more than five hours of long-distance flight when it departed, and may have flown to a more distant place. As for Nie Kai and others, they will still sail along the coast to explore today. The company originally planned to send a large team to search all the islands, but because the weather was clear yesterday and the aircraft had searched in great detail, there was no need to repeat the futile effort, so the decision was made to temporarily suspend the departure.

Reconnaissance Aircraft Aground, Damaged by Waves 127

As for the No. 19 Sikorsky aircraft, which was dispatched the day before yesterday to search for the missing aircraft, it ran aground and went missing. It was found anchored off Voloano Island and was subsequently hit by violent waves, causing the anchor chain to break suddenly, and drifting with the wind until it ran aground near Zhenhai. According to a telegram yesterday morning, the aircraft's wings and hull 2 were damaged due to the violent impact of the wind and waves, and it could not fly. The company decided to send a barge to tow it back for repairs within a few days. The pilots in the aircraft, Groschke and Sayler, have returned to Shanghai, while Huada and Mr. Lin are temporarily staying with the aircraft to guard it.

Shanghai-Chongqing Line Temporarily Reduced and Suspended 128

Yesterday, the China Aviation Corporation's Shanghai-Hankou flights were temporarily suspended because the Lockheed aircraft had to be dispatched to search for the missing aircraft and there were no other aircraft available. The Hankou-Chongqing line, which was originally scheduled for three flights per week, has now been reduced to two flights per week. The Shanghai-Beijing flights today will continue as usual. The Shanghai-Guangzhou line has been temporarily suspended pending the outcome of the search for the missing aircraft, after which it will be restored to its original state.

Jiangnan Railway Company to Complete Beijing-Wuhu Section This Year. Entire Beijing-Fujian Line to be Completed by End of 1937. Wuhu-Xuancheng Section to be Open to Traffic by End of Next Month. 132

The Jiangnan Railway Company held its first annual shareholders' meeting at the World Society Auditorium the day before yesterday. 147 shareholders and representatives attended. Supervisors were re-elected, and the increase of capital to $3 million and the completion of the entire Beijing-Fujian railway line were approved. The details are recorded below.

Shareholders' Meeting: The first annual shareholders' meeting of the Jiangnan Railway Company was held at 4:00 PM the day before yesterday. Shareholders and representatives, including Zhang Jingjiang, Li Shizeng, Ye Chucang, Zhang Xiaolin, Du Yuesheng, Yang Zhixiong, and others, totaling 147 people, attended. Chairman of the Board, Song Ziwen, was unable to attend due to other commitments and was represented by Zhang Xiaolin as acting chairman. (1) Reports: (A) Report on resolutions of previous board meetings; (B) Report on the 1932 account and the Lixin Accountant's certificate; (C) Engineering Report; (D) Director Li Shizeng insisted on resigning as chairman. The 21st Board of Directors meeting resolved to approve this resignation and publicly elected Director Song Ziwen to succeed as chairman of the board. (2) Matters for discussion: (A) Resolved to complete the entire Beijing-Fujian railway line in stages, temporarily postpone the construction of the Sunjiabu to Zhapu section, and complete the Beijing-Wuhu section by the end of this year in order to connect with the Shanghai-Nanjing Railway; (B) Resolved to increase capital to $3 million; (C) Resolved to amend Article 27 of the Articles of Association to increase the number of directors by four and supervisors by two in order to increase capital. Additional directors will be elected at a special shareholders' meeting; (D) Re-election of supervisors: Chu Minyi, Qin Daishi, Yang Zhixiong, Xu Guannan, Zhou Wenrui, Wei Bocong, Fang Yaoting, and seven others were elected.

Completion in Stages: When the company was founded, the original plan was to build the Wuhu-Zhapu Railway, from Wuhu in Anhui, through Xuancheng, Guangde, Wuxing, and Jiaxing, to Zhapu in Zhejiang. Since construction began last year, progress has been very rapid. The Wuhu to Zhusigang section has already been temporarily opened for ticketing. Subsequently, the company planned to extend the line north to Nanjing and south to Zhao'an on the Fujian border, with the approval of the Ministry of Railways. After detailed planning, this was submitted to the shareholders' meeting and it was resolved to complete it in four stages. It is expected that the Beijing-Wuhu section will be completed by the end of this year and connected to the Shanghai-Nanjing Railway. The Wuhu to Sunjiabu section will be completed in mid-May. By the end of 1935, it will be extended to Shexian (Huizhou). By the end of 1936, it will be connected to the Hangzhou-Jiangshan Railway. By the end of 1937, it will be built across the Xianxia Ridge from Yushan to Zhao'an on the Fujian border, and the entire line will be completed. The construction cost will increase to $3 million by the end of this year. More than $2.7 million of the capital has already been raised, and it will continue to be increased gradually in order to complete each stage of the project.

Active Construction: The section from Wuhu to Zhusigang has been temporarily opened to traffic, with only third-class tickets being sold. However, due to incomplete facilities, first-class passengers are charged a reduced fourth-class fare. According to the report from that location, the operating income is about $100 per day. The engineering vehicle has already been opened to Wanzi. According to the original plan, it can be built to Xuancheng this month. However, due to the delay in the bridge construction there, it must be completed in late May. At that time, a traffic opening ceremony will be held. At the same time, the Beijing-Wuhu section project is limited to completion before the end of this year. Therefore, the survey of the route started on the 25th of last month. The engineering department has limited the completion to the 5th of next month. Then the earthwork project can be tendered and started two months later. There is only one bridge in Dangtu in this section, which is also being planned and is planned to be built at the same time to avoid delaying the project.

The Case of Russian Vagrants Impersonating French Vice-Consul Continues to be Tried Yesterday. The Defendants' Statements are Cunning and Stubbornly Refuse to Tell the Truth. Because the Two Key Witnesses, Xu and Fan, Were Not Present, the Date was Changed. 133

Russian vagrants Raiviski, et al., previously impersonated French Vice-Consul and French Police General Inspector and Detective Chief, etc., falsely claiming to allow the establishment of gambling dens, defrauding Chinese Xu Haidu and Fan Gongru of huge sums. The French Police, together with the Chinese and Western detectives of the Joint Police Station, arrested the defendants at the Dante Moses Restaurant on March 28 of this year and sent them to the Second Special Court for trial. The details have been reported in this newspaper. Yesterday was the date for the continuation of the trial. The interrogation is recorded below.

Case Overview: Three Russian vagrants, Raiviski, Lawmanov, and Bobov, impersonated the French Vice-Consul, the French Police General Inspector, and the French Police Detective Chief, etc., colluding with accomplices Sheshenaufa and Laguri Avaladimir, etc., to defraud Xu Haidu, a Chinese resident in the Sun Temple area of ​​Zhabei (formerly worked in the sample room of the British Public Works Department and opened the Danggui First Stage Theater), on the grounds that they were allowed to establish a club gambling den within the French Concession, defrauding him of 30,000 yuan in activity expenses. Xu first paid 2,000 yuan. Fan Gongxu, a native of Zhenjiang, who lived at No. 5 Lishui Lane, Danshui Road, intended to open a kitchen in the gambling den and also paid Raiviski et al. 1,000 yuan. Xu et al. believed that the matter had been successful and rented a house at No. 3 Garden Lane, 634 Avenue Joffre, and started preparing for the layout.

Later, an accomplice secretly arranged for Xu and Fan to host a banquet for Raiviski et al. at the Dante Moses Restaurant on Sichuan Road at 7:00 PM on the 28th of last month, and invited Pan Jielu to invite Qian Chenglong, the chief translator of the French Police, to act as an interpreter. Qian detected the flaw and reported it to Fan Langdeng, the deputy inspector of the French Police, who led Western detectives Yang Gaoski and Ivanoff to report to the Joint Police Station and ordered Chinese and Western detectives to assist. Lai, Lao, Bao, and Si were arrested one after another and taken back to the police station and transferred to the Second Special District Local Court for interrogation and investigation. During the postponement, the accomplice Laguri Avramir was arrested, and a full set of roulette gambling equipment was found in his home and sent to the court for joint investigation. The details have been reported in the previous newspaper. Waiting outside the Dante Moses Restaurant, I went to the Dante Moses Restaurant, where Xu Haidu introduced me to Raiviski. Xu said that he was the French Vice-Consul Buerui. Xu also pointed to Lawmanov as the French General Inspector and Bobov as the Detective Chief. When taking a seat, Lai said that the Avenue Joffre No. 634 had been issued a shooting permit for six months and that any gambling game could be established in the future.

Demanding 30,000 yuan, it was necessary to lobby the French Consul General and the police station for 30,000 yuan, with 15,000 yuan for lobbying fees and 15,000 yuan for start-up fees, etc. I resigned without waiting for the end of the banquet and reported to the deputy inspector who was waiting outside the door, who immediately arrested the defendants, etc., said the official, ordering the 2nd, 3rd, 4th, 5th and 4th defendants to be taken down. According to the first defendant, Raiviski, he knew Xu Haidu and met him in January of this year at Lawmanov's house, introduced by Lao. Xu said that he had worked in the Public Works Department for 30 years. At that time, Lao said to Xu in French, "I am Bai Er Lai," but he did not say that he was a consul.

(Cigarette nickname) Bai Er Lai is my nickname, that is, the name of a cigarette. I met at Dante Moses on March 28. Qian Chenglong did not say to Qian that I was Vice-Consul Buerui. I met with Xu twice. The officer ordered the third defendant, Lawmanov, to be brought to court. According to the confession, he knew Xu Haidu for about four or five months, about December of last year or January of this year, but he didn't remember clearly. He introduced Xu to Raiviski, about on a road beside a car between a hotel on Avenue de France and the French Consulate.

(Adjourned for further hearing) At that time, I said to Xu, Raiviski Bai Er Lai, is Lai's nickname, which is a cigarette term. I didn't say that Lai was the French consul. Xu and Lai met twice. The first time was by the roadside, and the second time was the day of the arrest, etc. By this time, it was past noon. The court said that the witnesses were not complete and could not be tried, and announced that the hearing would be adjourned for another 20 days. The defendants were still sent back to prison separately. The defendants' lawyer then claimed that the police had finished investigating the defendants and requested that they be allowed to post bail pending trial. The officer said that the case was serious and that the defendants had not been fully interrogated. The request for bail was rejected. The defendants were then taken down by the bailiffs and sent back to the police station.

Dispute over the Transfer of Rende Hall by the Guangzhao Scaffolding Trade in Shanghai. Rende Hall Has a History of More Than 80 Years and Abundant Assets. The Old Officers Were Removed for Malpractice and the New Officers Must Have a Court Hearing to Collect the Funds. 134

The Rende Hall of the Shanghai Guangzhao Scaffolding Trade is organized by Cantonese carpenters. Its nature is similar to a trade union. It was founded during the Daoguang period of the Qing Dynasty and has a history of more than 80 years. It has always aimed to connect with the homeland and assist fellow tradesmen. Each year, several directors are elected to handle the hall's affairs. The hall's funds have always been collected from donations from fellow tradesmen and are quite sufficient. The funds accumulated over the years have been used to purchase real estate. Currently, there are two properties: one is the hall's address, and the other is the entire real estate of the North and South Rende Lane on Dongxi Huade Road. Due to the years of purchase, the value of the property has increased to

(more than 600,000) yuan. The regular expenses of the Rende Hall and the free school run by the hall are maintained by the income from the property. In 1931, the hall revised its regulations and formally reorganized according to the trade union method, abolishing the director system and adopting the committee system. However, when it was first registered with the Social Affairs Bureau, ambitious elements among the fellow tradesmen, who had long coveted the hall's huge assets, took the opportunity to collude with each other and forcibly take control. Those who kept themselves clean then retired and were unwilling to compete. Since then, each election has been held by these people to re-elect themselves.

Taking Advantage for Personal Gain 135

Last year, on the pretext of relieving unemployed fellow tradesmen, a few people advocated the unauthorized sale of all the real estate in the North and South Rende Lane, and the proceeds were freely disposed of. At that time, the Cantonese expatriates in Shanghai were all dissatisfied, and finally their undisclosed control aroused public anger. Then there was a request to the Social Affairs Bureau to withhold and investigate the funds deposited in the Hongkou Commercial Bank. As a result of the thorough investigation by the Social Affairs Bureau, it was determined that the hall's committee members Li Jiafu, Chen Yinbao, Qiu Shen, Li Jianfang, Zhu Jingcai, Huang Huibao, etc.

(unauthorized sale of public property) took the opportunity to commit malpractice, all of which were evidenced. Therefore, the bureau immediately ordered the hall to reorganize and, because fellow tradesman Lu Bingjie was quite trusted by the public, he was appointed to be responsible for convening a re-election meeting. Before the reorganization, Lu Bingjie was allowed to take over all the hall's affairs on a temporary basis, and the former illegal committee members were given a deadline to hand over the hall's affairs. Unexpectedly, Li Jiafu et al. hid the seals, account books, deeds, etc. and refused to hand them over. However, unemployed fellow tradesmen waiting to receive relief funds could not receive the funds and their hardships deepened. Lu Bingjie, in his capacity as a responsible person, repeatedly petitioned the Social Affairs Bureau on his behalf. With the approval of the bureau,

(Relief funds were issued first) A special notice was issued to Tong Bank to release the funds. Unexpectedly, Li et al. relied on the seized seals and sent a letter to the bank to stop payment. Because both parties had a dispute, the bank handed over all its deposits to the First Special District Local Court for safekeeping, pending legal resolution. On the 9th of last month, Lu convened a reorganization meeting according to the law, but Li et al. suddenly went to interfere and used lawyers as their amulet, tore up the meeting agenda and seized the meeting sign-in book, wantonly making trouble. After the suppression by Peng Zhenqiu and Rao Qiangsheng, representatives sent by the Social Affairs Bureau to monitor the meeting, Li et al. dispersed. The meeting was then opened. A total of

(270 fellow tradesmen attended) Under the guidance of the monitors, 11 organizing committee members were first elected to carry out the reorganization in advance. The meeting also passed resolutions to remove the illegal committee members Li Jiafu et al. from their posts and invalidate the old seals, and reported the resolutions to the Social Affairs Bureau for approval to put them into use. Soon after, they sent a letter to the First Special District Local Court, requesting that the funds deposited in the Tong Bank be returned to the hall for collection so as to relieve the unemployed fellow tradesmen. The special court then summoned them yesterday, and Judge Tao Dejun instructed the hall's representatives to transfer the deposit to Chen Enxian et al., the opposing party, who had filed a lawsuit. Before

(the judgment is confirmed), it is not convenient to issue the funds. If the procedures are legal, the reasons are sufficient, and there is sufficient evidence, they can be submitted at the future trial and await a fair hearing, etc. After the representatives of the teachers, they submitted a petition to the bureau, stating the circumstances of the court summons, and said that this matter originally belonged to a social group dispute, which should be handled by your bureau. Even if the opposing party does not agree, they can appeal to your court. However, they dare to play tricks and disrupt the government, causing litigation. Moreover, the unemployed fellow tradesmen are suffering from hunger and cold,

(leading and waiting for assistance) Fang Ji relief is on the way, and life can be turned from danger to safety. The factual report is submitted secretly to the court, requesting the court to hand over the hall's funds to the responsible persons of the hall's organizing committee for distribution. It is also heard that the First Special Court will also summon the two parties in Chen Enbao et al.'s case against Lu Bingjie et al. within days to continue the investigation so as to resolve it as soon as possible.

A Child Kicks a Strong Man to Death. A Naughty Student Causes a Major Disaster. A School Worker Dies Innocently. 136

Jinjiachao, Xijiu Village, Yangjing Town, Pudong, is a village. There is a Sanxiu Experimental Primary School. The students are all farmers' children and are extremely naughty. At about 9:00 AM yesterday (the 13th), the school opened and the students gathered. However, there was still half an hour before class. Therefore, a group of naughty children were competing with each other and fighting each other. There was a primary school student named Xu Zhiming, who was 13 years old. When he was fighting with another primary school student, Chen Da (43 years old), a worker from Changshu, happened to be sweeping the classroom. Seeing Xu Hai twisting people into a ball, he went to pull them apart. However, Xu Hai was naughty and stubborn, causing him to quarrel with Chen Da. Unexpectedly, Xu Zhiming kicked up a foot, and Chen Da didn't guard against it. He hit the vital part of his abdomen. Chen Da was injured and immediately fell to the ground. He cried out miserably and died of breath. The principal of the school was shocked when he learned about it. He immediately detained Xu Hai and reported it to the Jinjiachao Police Station of the Third District and Second Sub-bureau. He took Xu Hai out and sent him to the Third District and Second Sub-bureau. He found that it was rare for a child to kick a strong man to death. In addition to summoning his parents, Yang Musheng, the local guarantee of the 44th Map of Nian Erbao, was ordered to report to the local court for a post-mortem examination in the afternoon. The prosecutor will cross the Pu River today to investigate the matter.

The Cadres Arrested at the Wusong Machine Factory Will Be Released Within Days. The Two-Route Special Party Department Sends a Letter to the Garrison Command Stating the Facts. 140

The cadres of the Wusong Machine Factory Trade Union Office of the Two Routes were arrested by the Road Bureau and sent to the Garrison Command on March 30. It has been nearly two weeks since then. It is learned that the Two-Route Special Party Department, in order to seek a proper solution to this case as soon as possible, "has separately telegraphed the Central Executive Committee, the Central Organization Committee, and Chairman Chiang, and the Ministry of Railways, and sent a letter to the Songhu Garrison Command, stating the truth of the facts and instructing the release of the innocent." The details are recorded as follows.

Reply to the Garrison Headquarters 141

A letter from the Two-Route Special Party Headquarters replying to the Garrison Headquarters states: In reply to your department's legal document number 756, which contained a letter from the Beijing-Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railway Administration regarding the arrest of eleven suspected counter-revolutionaries, including Cao Wenkui, etc., the matter has been referred to the military law office for investigation according to the law. However, it is crucial to conduct a detailed investigation into the defendants' usual behavior and whether they have committed any crimes, to ensure a fair trial. Therefore, we request that you investigate the following four points in detail and reply to us for further action. We also wish to maintain our official relationship. Herein, we first describe the facts and provide answers to the inquiries and contribute our opinions for your reference. We enclose a letter for your review and fair handling. We also wish to maintain our official relationship.

Detailed Account of the Facts 142

On February 19th of last year, our headquarters received a report from the Wusong Machinery Factory Branch of the Railway Workers' Union, transferred by the Railway Union, alleging that Mo Heng, the chief of the General Affairs Department and the Materials Department of the railway, was slandering the Party and the nation, undermining the labor movement, abusing his power, and engaging in private corruption. We immediately dispatched personnel to pay attention to the workers' speeches and requested the Railway Administration to resolve the matter publicly. However, party departments and workers' unions at all levels along the two railways successively filed complaints against Mo Heng, petitioned the Railway Administration for a solution, but to no avail. The public sentiment was agitated, and there was an informal work stoppage. Subsequently, our headquarters, fearing that counter-revolutionaries would seize the opportunity during the Fujian Incident, reported the matter to the Central Party Headquarters and requested the Ministry of Railways to send personnel to conduct a thorough investigation and handle the matter fairly. At the same time, we made every effort to persuade the workers, who fortunately understood the importance of the situation and quickly restored normal work conditions. As for Mo Heng's abuse of power, private corruption, slander of the Party and the nation, and undermining of the labor movement, we are still awaiting a fair investigation and handling by the Central Government and the Ministry of Railways. This is a general overview of the case.

Answering Each Question in Detail 143

(1) Are Cao Wenkui, Xu Shanqing, Li Kuikui, Lin Jinlin, Zhou Weixian, Han Weiyu, Chen Shusheng, Shi Zhenyuan, He Laixing, and Tang Genfa all cadres of the Wusong Machinery Factory Branch of the Two-Route Railway Workers' Union? Is their usual behavior honest, and do they have any counter-revolutionary leanings? After investigation, the above-mentioned people are indeed cadres of the Wusong Machinery Factory Branch of the Two-Route Railway Workers' Union. Among them, Xu Shanqing, Chen Shusheng, and He Laixing are members of our party, and Li Kuikui, Shi Zhenyuan, and Cao Wenkui are probationary members of our party. Their usual behavior is very honest, they work very hard, and they have no counter-revolutionary leanings. (2) Was the work slowdown by the factory workers in December of last year incited by these cadres, and was there any obstruction of military transport or collusion with the Fujian rebels? The informal work stoppage by the workers of the Wusong Machinery Factory in December of last year was entirely caused by Mo Heng, the chief of the General Affairs Department and the Materials Department of the railway, who slandered the Party and the nation, undermined the labor movement, abused his power, and engaged in private corruption. Party departments and workers' unions at all levels along the two railways all filed complaints against Mo Heng. The workers of the factory, due to their direct involvement, waited for Mo Heng to come to the factory to explain the situation. This was not something that the cadres could incite. Moreover, with over a thousand workers in the Wusong Machinery Factory, inciting a work slowdown was beyond the power of these cadres. As for obstructing military transport, it is absolutely not true. The Railway Administration informed our headquarters only that it almost obstructed military transport, so there was no actual implementation of obstructing military transport. Furthermore, the Wusong Machinery Factory specializes in repairing machinery and has nothing to do with train operations. How could there be any talk of obstructing military transport? In addition, during the Fujian rebellion, the employees of the two railways were deeply indignant. Mo Heng slandered the Party and the nation and undermined the labor movement. The workers believed that Mo Heng's words and actions were helping to fuel the rebellion, so they filed complaints against him, which was actually to eliminate counter-revolution. How could they collude with the Fujian rebels? The fact that our headquarters, considering the severity of the situation, persuaded the workers to resume work, and the workers immediately accepted, proves that they had no such intentions or actions. (3) Did Cao Wenkui and others incite Shanghai locomotive workers to go on strike during the work slowdown last year? Cao Wenkui and others are loyal members who work hard for party affairs and the labor movement, with outstanding results. When the Song Factory incident occurred, they regretted it themselves. The Shanghai locomotive workers sympathized with the Wusong workers for Mo Heng's improper measures, but there was no consistent trend. Moreover, this kind of expression of sympathy was not limited to the Shanghai locomotive workers; all employees of the railway had the same feeling. The facts are all there and can be verified. Our headquarters has not heard of this, nor is there any fact that can give rise to suspicion. If it is said that Cao Wenkui and others had the suspicion of inciting, then it is really an unfounded accusation. (Enclosed are letters and telegrams from subordinate party departments and branch offices, which have already been published in various newspapers, so they are omitted.) (4) Was the beating of newly dispatched officials and committee members of the Railway Administration by the cadres, or were they the instigators? The cadres have a deep faith in our party and are responsible for reporting news to standing committee member Chen Jiansu and special commissioner Cheng Shi. When Standing Committee Member Chen was hit by objects thrown by a small number of workers, most of the cadres were next to Committee Member Chen and stepped forward to protect him at the risk of their own lives. Several of them were also injured as a result. It is unreasonable to say that they were the instigators, and their actions are not allowed by the facts.

Filing Complaints and Being Beaten Are Two Separate Matters 144

Last year's case of the Wusong Machinery Factory filing complaints against Mo Heng was purely due to Mo Heng's abuse of power, private corruption, slander of the Party and the nation, and undermining of the labor movement. The statements he made and the various points he reported before and after, as well as the results of the investigations by the Central Government and the Ministry of Railways, all prove that there was no counter-revolutionary behavior or facts. Our headquarters is close by, and we will never tolerate counter-revolutionaries. We have previously reported this in detail to the Central Government and the Ministry of Railways, requesting a fair investigation and handling. Three months have passed since the incident, and any emergency measures would not have been delayed until now. This time, the Railway Administration sent Qiu and Wang to the Song Factory to explain the situation to the workers together with our standing committee member Chen Chengshi in his personal capacity, and as a result, they were beaten. The Railway Administration took the opportunity to retaliate, which is very inappropriate. Not only does our headquarters believe that last year's case of filing complaints against Mo Heng and this time's case of Committee Member Chen Chengshi being beaten are two completely separate matters, but on the afternoon of the arrest of all the cadres of the factory, our headquarters sent Standing Committee Member Chen to ask the Railway Administration for the reason for the arrest. When Chen Bohua and Xue Jie, directors of the Two-Route Workers' Union, went to inquire, Director Huang repeatedly stated that the two cases were judged separately. Cao Wenkui was framed for supporting the Party and the nation and reporting corruption, which is even more unjust. We respectfully hope that you will investigate in detail and handle the matter fairly.

Arrested Directors to Be Released Within Days 145

Cao Wenkui, Lin Jinlin, Li Kuikui, Tang Genfa, Xu Shanqing, Shi Genfa, Han Weiyu, Zhou Weixian, Chen Shusheng, He Laixing, etc., cadres of the Wusong Machinery Factory Workers' Union Office, were arrested by the Railway Administration's railway police and the Public Security Bureau police on March 30th and escorted onto a car to the Garrison Headquarters. Subsequently, the Two-Route Workers' Union, the Two-Route Special Party Headquarters, etc., petitioned the Central Government to order the Ministry of Railways to handle the matter fairly. At the same time, they sent personnel to the Garrison Headquarters to explain the facts orally and in writing. According to news released by the Two-Route Party Headquarters yesterday, the Central Government has already ordered the Garrison Headquarters to allow bail. It is expected that they will be able to regain their freedom within days.

Municipal Zoo Initiates First Dairy Cow Competition Scheduled for May 27th at Penglai Market Winners to Receive Certificates, Best to Receive Trophy 146

The Shanghai Municipal Zoo, to promote the public's production undertakings and improve the breed of dairy cows, has launched the first dairy cow competition. It has now been approved by the Municipal Education Bureau and has formulated detailed rules and regulations and competition guidelines. The details are listed below:

Three Types of Dairy Cow Evaluation Methods 147

The competition rules and regulations are as follows: (Article 1) The name of the event is the First Dairy Cow Competition of the Shanghai Municipal Zoo. (Article 2) The purpose of the event is to promote the public's production undertakings and improve the breed of dairy cows. (Article 3) Exhibitors are limited to those of Chinese nationality. (Article 4) Exhibitors are limited to one cow of each breed. Excellent bulls may also participate in the exhibition. (Article 6) The event will hire several experts to serve as judges. Judges may not be exhibitors. (Article 7) Judging is classified by breed and is tentatively divided into three groups: Holstein, Jersey, and Guernsey. (Article 8) Judging scores will be based on a comparative method, with body shape accounting for 70%, milk quantity accounting for 15%, and milk quality accounting for 15%.

Address and Competition Date Determined 148

(Article 9) Exhibitors who score 60 or more points will be given a certificate by the event organizer. The exhibitor with the highest score will be given a trophy. In addition, prizes may be solicited from various institutions and individuals and distributed accordingly. (Article 10) The event will be held on May 27th of the 23rd year of the Republic. If it rains, it will be postponed by one week. (Article 11) The event will be held at the vacant space in the Penglai Market in Xiaoximen. (Article 12) All expenses of the event will be paid from the regular expenses of the Municipal Zoo. (Article 13) These regulations will be implemented after being approved by the Education Bureau.

Competition Guidelines Require Prior Registration 149

(1) Registration for exhibits will begin on April 20th and end on May 20th. (2) Before 1:00 PM on May 27th, contestants must bring their participating dairy cows and registration certificates to the venue to report and receive their venue number. (3) For the sake of solemnity, cow feed on the opening day will be provided by the cow owners themselves. (4) Cow owners must assign herdsmen to the venue to take care of the cows on the opening day and bring a milking bucket for milking during the competition. The milk will then be handed over to the judges to weigh and verify the amount of milk. (5) If you wish to arrange various publicity items related to publicity in the venue, you must report to the zoo for permission in advance.

Measures to Sanction Fellow Traders Not Joining Guild Shanghai Chamber of Commerce Requests Further Instructions 150

The Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce, based on the joint presentation of various industries that fellow traders refuse to join the association, thus the organization of fellow trade associations cannot be sound, had previously requested the Ministry of Industry to formulate measures to sanction those who do not join the association to control the economy and other conditions. It has been recorded in previous reports. It is now known that the Ministry of Industry has approved the guild's request, stating that it has no right to formulate sanctioning measures itself. The guild should, based on the "Nanjing Industrial and Commercial Guild Law" drafted by the Ministry, "After the Social Affairs Bureau verifies that the same-trade companies have not completed the membership registration procedures, they will be punished in accordance with the Administrative Execution Law." Report to the Ministry of Industry whether to use it or not. The two original texts of the approval and presentation are divided as follows:

The approval of the Ministry of Industry has been fully understood. The establishment of industrial and commercial associations is based on Article 2 of the Industrial and Commercial Association Law, which aims to maintain and enhance the public interests of the same industry. Companies and businesses should be happy to comply. Therefore, Article 7 of the same law only mentions that they should be members, and there are no provisions for sanctioning those who are not members. Moreover, since the law has not granted this Ministry the power to formulate implementation measures, this Ministry shall not formulate them without authorization. The previous presentation from the Chamber of Commerce has already been clearly instructed. It should still be handled in accordance with the previous order. This order.

The presentation of the Municipal Chamber of Commerce is for the purpose of presenting matters. It is found that the explanation requested by the subordinate association last time refers to the fact that if it has not joined the association, it cannot be punished in accordance with the articles of association, which seems to be different from the tone of the approval of your department this time. However, based on what your department said that the law has not granted the power to implement the measures, according to the Central Daily News published on March 25 this year, the Nanjing Industrial and Commercial Guild, which was jointly drafted by the Central Mass Movement Committee and the Social Affairs Bureau of your department and approved for record, the Provisional Measures for Re-election or Reorganization in accordance with the law, Article 5 of which states, "Companies and businesses in the same industry shall join the guild as members in accordance with the law. Those who have not yet joined the guild shall complete the registration within the time limit notified by each guild." Article 6 also states, "After each guild handles the supplementary registration, if there are still companies in the same industry that have not completed the membership registration procedures, they will be submitted to the Social Affairs Bureau for verification and punished in accordance with the Administrative Execution Law, and the business license of the company may be revoked." Based on the above situation, the power to deal with companies that refuse to join the association lies with the official government, and there are precedents. The affairs of Beijing and Shanghai are the same. Whether or not to follow the example, the reasoning is combined to write a presentation to your department for review, and the government gives approval and obeys. If it is deemed feasible, please also order the Shanghai Social Affairs Bureau to handle it, which is really convenient for the public.

The Central Mint Review Committee held its twelfth regular meeting in the auditorium on the third floor of the Central Bank on the Bund at 4:30 PM yesterday. The details are as follows:

Committee Members Present Yesterday committee members Kong Xiangxi, Chen Hang, Xu Jiying, Ye Fuxiao, Chen Guangfu, Qin Runqing, Hu Yunzhuang, Wu Yunzhai, Ye Zhuotang, Xi Demao, Lai Nalaiai, Aisi Dai Jinfu, Taiwan, Hu Mengjia, Shi Huang, etc., Those who asked for leave: Li Fuxun, Shi Bimen, Tang Shoumin, Qian Xinzhi, Xu Xinliu, etc., Attendants: Deputy Director of the Central Mint Wei Jingzhou, Secretary Qiao Fusan, chaired by Kong Xiangxi.

In addition to listing and announcing, it has also reported to the Ministry of Finance for record and publication in the Financial Daily. It has been replied that the review and chemical experiment manuscripts should be provided as much as possible, and it is not necessary to send personnel to handle the case together. (4) Approved the Central Mint's letter stating that on March 22, production was suspended for six hours due to the explosion of the wind pipe, and it was decided to work full-time on the 25th (Sunday) to supplement the products, etc. The committee worked as usual on that day, tested the products it cast, checked and sealed them for transportation. (5) The Central Mint sent four packages of silver cake samples directly allocated and melted by the Bao Yuan of the factory, with a list attached, requesting that they be chemically tested. The Chemical Experiment Department has been handed over to carry out chemical experiments, publish a table and reply to the factory. (6) The various forms of the accounting part of the Central Mint in January and February were sent to request a review, and all have been carefully reviewed. Another report: (7) The work report of the committee in February, the number of new currency factory strips reviewed, and the review of the silver account part have been compiled and sent to the Ministry of Finance for record along with various single tables. (8) The accounting part forms sent by the Central Mint for review, including 5 copies in January, 7 copies in February, and 21 copies of silver ingot and melting reports and Class B factory strip casting reports successively sent to the meeting in March, and 1 copy of the Class B factory strip weekly report, have been consulted in accordance with the items opened on the table. After the factory's account books were completed, the summary of the accounts is explained below.

Total Number Cast (1) Casting New Currency and Factory Strips It was found that new coins were cast for 21 days in February, with a total of 3,921,340 yuan cast, with an average of 186,730 yuan per day. The number transferred to the Central Bank was 3,900,000 yuan, which is in line with the number of qualified reviews by the committee in February. In addition, 3,458 880 factory strips were produced (3,400 strips were transferred to the Central Bank), which is in line with those stamped by the committee. (2) Name of Silver and Amount of Copper Used It was found that the factory sent daily silver ingot melting reports (regarding the one-yuan silver part) and Class B factory strip casting reports in February, which have been individually calculated and compiled. One report form was made, with a total gross weight of 10,468,452.52 ounces of silver and copper melted in the one-yuan silver part, and a total gross weight of 3,976,859.18 ounces of silver and copper melted in the Class B factory strip part.

Chemical Experiment Report The Chemical Experiment Department reported that the number of new coins cast by the Central Mint in March and sent to the committee for review totaled 5.8 million yuan. 630 yuan was drawn out for chemical experiments in accordance with the regulations. The average fineness was 880.33, which was 0.33 higher than the legal standard, and the weight was 26.6925 grams, which was about 2/10,000 lower than the legal weight. Both were within the legal tolerance. In the same month, 4,439 Class B factory strips with a fineness of 880 were also stamped by the chemical experimenter with the committee's stamp at the time of proofreading.

Tea Export Situation in the First Quarter of This Year More Than 5,000 Quintals Less Than the Same Quarter Last Year Green Tea Increased Slightly Other Tea Exports Decreased 154

According to the Shanghai Commodity Inspection Bureau of the Ministry of Industry, the quantity of tea exported and transshipped in the first quarter of this year (from January to March) was 72,623.67 quintals (1 quintal is equal to 1.6535 dan in the old system), compared with 77,769.66 quintals in the same quarter last year, a decrease of more than 5,000 quintals. Among them, those directly exported from Shanghai were 25,131.75 quintals, a decrease of about 1,400 quintals (26,479.74 quintals last year), and those transshipped from this port were 47,491.92 quintals, a decrease of nearly 4,000 quintals (51,289.92 quintals last year). In terms of tea exports, green tea accounted for 21,046.20 quintals, an increase of about 900 quintals compared with last year (20,181.09 quintals). Black tea exports were 4,825.86 quintals, a decrease compared with last year (5,319.02 quintals) of about 500 quintals. Brick tea exports were 45,021.28 quintals, the largest decrease, reaching 3,600 quintals. The output of other teas was also 1,800 quintals less. In terms of exports to other countries, except for a slight increase in the United Kingdom, the rest have declined, especially Russia and the United States. The transaction of foreign tea in the spring is usually idle. Last year's export increase was due to the resumption of diplomatic relations between China and Russia, which happened to be the opportunity, and the export of brick tea increased greatly. Since the beginning of this year, the tea market abroad has been sluggish, and the accumulation in Africa is relatively abundant, resulting in a sharp drop in tea prices and a standstill in transactions. Although exports are less than last year, they are still more than in the previous year, because it was rumored in February that the French government would increase tea taxes from April, so tea merchants actively loaded and transported to avoid the loss of increased taxes.

Anecdotes About Pan Lanshi After His Death 156

Pan Lanshi, a famous scholar in Lingnan, was seventy-six years old this year. He was in good spirits, but he died suddenly due to a stroke after falling. Those who heard about it regretted it. There are quite a few things to say about his funeral. (1) Pan had many writings in his life, and in recent years he selected them into ten volumes, which were published by his disciple Tan Junren. A clear copy was completed a few days ago, and he personally discussed the final draft with Yao Jun Yuqin. He died suddenly on the evening of his return, which is very strange. (2) Pan was very devout in Buddhism in his daily life. A few days ago, he wrote the four words "Let go of everything" and gave them to his friend Ling Jun, and firmly instructed his family members not to cry when he died, but to recite the name of Buddha in unison, and could not move until eight hours later. His family has followed his orders. This is another matter. (3) There were many male and female disciples. They privately called Pan "Mr. Jingyi". Pan was upright throughout his life and did not seek fame and fortune. He lived in Shanghai for forty years and made a living by selling his writings. He also did not like to associate with wealthy people. Those who commented said that the two words "Jingyi" could be worth Pan's guilt. Pan had three sons, the eldest doing business in Hong Kong, the second working as an assistant in a Western medical clinic in Hong Kong, and the third working in the Qiongzhou Customs. This time, Pan went from illness to death. His family and friends sent three telegrams to Hong Kong urging him to come, and only received a reply of "Abandoning his job and coming to Shanghai, he would have nothing to eat" eight words. It was not possible to help him with the funeral by helping his relatives and friends. It is said that in this time of moral decay, it is not surprising that the father's death is not cared for. Only the eight words in the telegram are very humorous. Fortunately, Pan was broad-minded before his death, even if he had this order, he might not be able to close his eyes, cloud.

Then, discussions began: (1) A letter from the Municipal United Seven District Branch regarding member Tong Yaode's request for negotiation due to uneven rent was resolved to be handled by the Mediation Office; (2) Zhou Fuzhang's letter requesting assistance due to landlords pursuing arrears was resolved as follows: (A) Send a letter to the landlord for explanation; (B) Instruct Zhou Fuzhang to transcribe the landlord's letter and send it to the committee; (3) Fu Jide's letter requesting reference to the Nanjing City Rent Regulations approved by the Central Political Committee and ratified by the Executive Yuan, and proceeding with similar support was resolved to submit to the Executive Yuan for approval; (4) A letter from the Municipal United Twenty-One District Branch regarding Xu Yunhui's proposal to request the Public Works Department to investigate empty houses within its jurisdiction, set a minimum period for renting, and levy property taxes according to the assessed value to prevent stubbornness; otherwise, various legal entities should jointly organize beggar rehabilitation centers with the Public Works Department. It was resolved to first investigate empty houses throughout the city and then review and handle; (5) A branch of Yuequnfang regarding landlords pursuing arrears or taking legal action was resolved to forward a letter to the landlord; (6) Disputes in the South City District Committee were resolved to send personnel to investigate the truth and then review; (7) Nine branches including Hongshoufang requested relief from landlord oppression, and it was resolved to forward a letter to the landlord to stop illegal actions; (8) A letter from the Zhabei District Committee requesting prompt implementation of a large-scale petition was resolved to review after the Municipal Government's reply; (9) The Huadelu Weichangli branch requested registration, and it was resolved to approve the registration.

International Trade Bureau Introduces Fruit Sales to Liverpool 158

According to the International Trade Bureau yesterday, the Commercial Section of the Consulate in Liverpool specifically requested the Bureau to introduce the export of national fruit for promotion. The Bureau immediately conveyed this to various fruit merchants in this port. New Initiatives of the Chinese Wrestling Association 160

The Chinese Wrestling Association is an organization dedicated to promoting and publicizing the national art of wrestling. It was established in June of last year. Although it has not been long, its achievements have been remarkable. Recently, in view of the fact that wrestling has been adopted as one of the physical education textbooks for middle schools by the Textbook Compilation Committee of the Ministry of Education, but there are not many books on wrestling research in China, the president of the association, the famous martial artist Tong Zhongyi, has compiled a book on Chinese wrestling methods, with photography and printing by the up-and-coming artist Hong Zhifang. The book elaborates on wrestling methods and the principles of force in a very thorough manner. Enthusiastic physical educators, such as party and state figures Chu Minyi and Zhang Zhijiang, director of the Central Guoshu Institute, have highly praised it and have presented calligraphic prefaces. It is said that it is currently being typeset and printed and will be published next month. Another book, "Wrestling Competition Refereeing Method," is being compiled by Zhang Weichuan, a member of the association. After the manuscript is completed, it will be submitted to the Central Guoshu Institute for review and will be released.
